PREFACE
         This code of the City of Virginia, as supplemented, contains
ordinances up to and including ordinance 2025-6 passed June 9, 2025. Ordinances
of the City adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code
to the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the
City office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code
has been amended, superseded or repealed.
                     American Legal Publishing
                     Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they have not been incorporated into
the code and they may not show the original ordinances in their entirety.
Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions concerning
the ordinances listed.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE NO. 09-16
An ordinance adopting and enacting a new code for the city of Virginia,
Illinois; providing for the repeal of certain ordinances not included therein;
providing a penalty for the violation thereof; providing for the manner of
amending such code; and providing when such code and this ordinance shall
become effective.
   Whereas, the mayor, with the approval of the city council, has caused a new
code to be published in typewritten form;
   Whereas, the new code updates and clarifies various ordinances lawfully
passed by the Virginia city council in years past and also eliminates
inconsistent and archaic ordinances, or parts of ordinances, not applicable to
the existing conditions of the city;
   Whereas, it has been determined the new code will better protect individual
rights of due process by these clarifications;
   THEREFORE, be it ordained by the city council of the city of Virginia,
Illinois, as follows:
   Section 1. The code entitled "City Code Of Virginia, Illinois," published by
Sterling Codifiers, consisting of titles 1 through 11, each inclusive, is
adopted.
   Section 2. All ordinances of a general and permanent nature enacted on or
before March 9, 2009, and not included in the code or recognized and continued
in force by reference therein, are repealed.
   Section 3. The repeal provided for in section 2 hereof shall not be
construed to revive any ordinance or part thereof that has been repealed by a
subsequent ordinance that is repealed by this ordinance.
   Section 4. Unless another penalty is expressly provided, every person
convicted of a violation of any provision of the code or any ordinance, rule or
regulation adopted or issued in pursuance thereof shall be punished by a fine
not exceeding $750.00. Each act of violation and each day upon which any such
violation shall occur shall constitute a separate offense. The penalty provided
by this section, unless another penalty is expressly provided, shall apply to
the amendment of any code section, whether or not such penalty is reenacted in
the amendatory ordinance. In addition to the penalty prescribed above, the city
may pursue other remedies such as abatement of nuisances, injunctive relief and
revocation of licenses or permits.
   Section 5. Additions or amendments to the code when passed in such form as
to indicate the intention of the city council to make the same a part of the
code shall be deemed to be incorporated in the code, so that reference to the
code includes the additions and amendments.
   Section 6. Ordinances adopted after March 9, 2009, that amend or refer to
ordinances that have been codified in the code shall be construed as if they
amend or refer to like provisions of the code.
   Section 7. This ordinance shall become effective upon passage.
   Passed by the city council of the city of Virginia, Illinois, at a regular
meeting thereof held on the 12th day of October 2009, and approved by the mayor
on the same day.
AYES  5 NAYS  0 ABSENT  1
 
   /s/  Steve Sudbrink, Mayor
ATTEST:
   /s/  Sarah Fanning, City Clerk   
TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
VIRGINIA CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Custody Of City Code
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon adoption by the city council, this code is hereby declared to be and shall
hereafter constitute the official city code of the city of Virginia. This code
of ordinances shall be known and cited as the VIRGINIA CITY CODE, and it is
hereby published by authority of the city council and shall be kept up to date
as provided in section
1-1-3 of this chapter under the direction of the city attorney, acting for the
city council. Any reference to the number of any section contained herein shall
be understood to refer to the position of the same number, its appropriate
chapter and title heading, and to the general penalty clause relating thereto,
as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to this code by title
in any legal documents. (1981 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
This code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in all administrative tribunals of the
state as the ordinances of the city of a general and permanent effect, except
the excluded ordinances enumerated in section
1-2-1 of this title. (1981 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
When any ordinance or part thereof shall be repealed, modified or amended by
subsequent ordinance, the ordinance or part thereof so repealed, modified or
amended shall continue in force until the taking effect of the ordinance so
repealing, modifying or amending the same. No ordinance or part thereof
repealed by the city council shall be deemed to be revised by the repeal of the
repealing ordinance unless it shall therein so expressly provide. All
ordinances passed by the city council shall be deposited in the office of the
city clerk and shall be duly recorded by the clerk in a book known as the
"ordinance record" and appropriately indexed by titles or subject matters. The
city clerk shall file and carefully preserve the original of all ordinances so
deposited in his office. (1925 Code § 13-2)
1-1-4: CUSTODY OF CITY CODE:
All the printed code books shall be deposited with the city clerk who shall
deliver one copy thereof to each officer of the city, taking receipt therefor
and charge the same to such officer. Said officer shall, at the expiration of
his term of office, return the same to the city clerk. (1925 Code § 38-8)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Proceedings Under Former Ordinances Valid
1-2-4: Conflicting Provisions
1-2-5: Severability
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the city passed by the mayor and city council prior
to the adoption of this code are hereby repealed, except such as are included
in this code or are by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal
(subject to the saving clauses contained in the following sections), and
excluding the following ordinances which are not hereby repealed:
   A.   Tax levy ordinances;
   B.   Appropriation ordinances;
   C.   Ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations;
   D.   Franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to
persons or corporations;
   E.   Contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants;
   F.   Salary ordinances;
   G.   Ordinances establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other
public places;
   H.   Improvement ordinances;
   I.   Bond ordinances;
   J.   Ordinances relating to elections;
   K.   Ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or
from the city; and
   L.   All special ordinances. (1981 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroad crossings with streets and other public ways,
or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities shall
be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this code or by virtue of the section
1-2-1 of this chapter, excepting as this code may contain provisions for such
matters, in which case, this code shall be considered as amending such
ordinance or ordinances in respect to such provisions only. (1981 Code)
1-2-3: PROCEEDINGS UNDER FORMER ORDINANCES VALID:
No suit, proceeding, fine, forfeiture, penalty, debt, right or liability
whatsoever instituted, incurred, created, given or accrued by or under any
ordinance of the city prior to its repeal or modification shall be annulled,
released, discharged or in any way affected by the passage of such repealing,
modifying or amending ordinances; but the same may be prosecuted, recovered,
completed and enjoined as fully in all respects as if such ordinance or part
thereof had remained in full force, unless otherwise expressly provided in the
ordinance making such repeal, modification or amendment. (1925 Code § 13-7)
1-2-4: CONFLICTING PROVISIONS:
When the provisions of different ordinances or of the different chapters of any
ordinance conflict with or contravene each other, the provisions and
requirements of each ordinance or chapter shall prevail as to all subjects,
matters and questions embraced within or arising out of the subject matter
thereof. But if different or conflicting provisions be found in different
sections of the same ordinance or chapter, the provisions of the section last
in numerical order shall prevail, unless such construction would be repugnant
or inconsistent with the obvious meaning and intent of such ordinance or
chapter. (1925 Code § 8-3)
1-2-5: SEVERABILITY:
The invalidity of any portion or any section of this code shall not affect the
validity of any other portion or section which can be executed without such
invalid part. (1925 Code § 38-7)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS; INTERPRETATION
SECTION:
1-3-1: General Rules Of Interpretation
1-3-2: General Definitions
1-3-3: Catchlines
1-3-1: GENERAL RULES OF INTERPRETATION:
   A.   Liberal Construction: All general provisions, terms, phrases and
expressions contained in this code shall be liberally construed in order that
the true intent and meaning of the mayor and city council may be fully carried
out.
   B.   Minimum Requirements: In the interpretation and application of any
provision of this code, it shall be held to be the minimum requirements adopted
for the promotion of the public health, safety and general welfare.
   C.   Computation Of Time: Whenever a notice is required to be given or an
act to be done in a certain length of time before any proceeding shall be held,
the day on which such notice is given or such act is done shall not be counted
in computing the time, but the day on which such proceeding is to be held shall
be counted.
   D.   Delegation Of Authority: Whenever a provision appears requiring the
head of a department or some other city officer to do some act or perform some
duty, it is to be construed to authorize the head of the department or other
officer to designate, delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the
required act or perform the duty unless the terms of the provision or section
specify otherwise.
   E.   Gender: A word importing the masculine gender only shall extend and be
applied to females and to firms, partnerships and corporations as well as to
males.
   F.   Joint Authority: All words giving a joint authority to three (3) or
more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a
majority of such persons or officers.
   G.   May; Shall: The word "may" is permissive; the word "shall" is
mandatory.
   H.   Nontechnical And Technical Words: Words and phrases shall be construed
according to the common and approved usage of the language, but technical words
and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
meaning in law shall be construed and understood according to such meaning.
   I.   Number: A word importing the singular number only may extend and be
applied to several persons and things as well as to one person and thing.
   J.   Officers And Employees Generally: Whenever any officer or employee is
referred to by title only, such reference shall be construed as if followed by
the words "of the city of Virginia".
   K.   Tense: Words used in the past or present tense include the future as
well as the past and present.
   L.   Ordinance: The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the city
has been changed in the content of this code to "title", "chapter", "section"
and/or "subsection" or words of like import for organizational and
clarification purposes only. Such change to city ordinances is not meant to
amend passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (2009 Code)
1-3-2: GENERAL DEFINITIONS:
Whenever the following words or terms are used in this code, they shall have
such meanings herein ascribed to them, unless the context makes such meaning
repugnant thereto:
AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another.
CITY: The city of Virginia, county of Cass, state of Illinois.
CODE: The city code of the city of Virginia.
COUNCIL: Unless otherwise indicated, the city council of the city of Virginia.
COUNTY: The county of Cass, state of Illinois.
FEE: A sum of money charged by the city for the carrying on of a business,
profession or occupation.
LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, profession
or occupation.
MISDEMEANOR: Any offense for which a sentence to a term of imprisonment in
other than a penitentiary for less than one year may be imposed.
NUISANCE: Anything offensive or obnoxious to the health and welfare of the
inhabitants of the city; or any act or thing repugnant to, or creating a hazard
to, or having a detrimental effect on the property of another person or to the
community.
OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this code or the omission of any
act required by the provisions of this code.
OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or profession.
OWNER: As applied to a building or land, shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
PERSON: Any public or private corporation, firm, partnership, association,
organization, government or any other group acting as a unit, as well as a
natural person.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Shall include every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished, and every right or
interest therein.
RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate
to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things in small quantities
direct to the consumer.
RIGHT OF WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
STATE: The state of Illinois.
STREET: Shall include alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
TENANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who occupies
the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with others.
WHOLESALER, WHOLESALE DEALER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be
understood to relate to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things in
quantity to persons who purchase for the purpose of resale.
WRITTEN, IN WRITING: May include printing and any other mode of representing
words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by
law to any official or public writing or bond required by law, it shall be in
the proper handwriting of such person, or in case he is unable to write, by his
proper mark. (1981 Code; amd. 2009 Code)
1-3-3: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of this code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when
any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. (1981
Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application Of Provisions
1-4-3: Liability Of Officers
1-4-4: Collection Of Attorney Fees
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY 1 :
   A.   General Penalty Imposed: Unless specifically provided elsewhere in this
code or state statute, any person found to have been in violation of any of the
terms and provisions of this code shall be fined in an amount not to exceed
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). No imprisonment for failure to pay such
fine, penalty or cost shall exceed six (6) months for each offense. Each day
that a violation continues shall be deemed to be a separate offense. A penalty
for each offense may include a requirement that the offending party perform
some reasonable public service work such as, but not limited to, picking up
litter in public parks or upon public highways or performing maintenance of
public facilities. A violation hereof may be established by a preponderance of
the evidence.
   B.   Acts Consistent With Criminal Laws Of State: If, by the terms of an
ordinance, an act that would be consistent with the criminal laws of the state
is declared to be a misdemeanor, the penalty therefor shall be for a period of
incarceration in a penal institution other than the penitentiary not to exceed
six (6) months. The matter shall be prosecuted under the rules of criminal
procedure of the state, and the city shall be required to establish guilt
beyond a reasonable doubt.
   C.   Limitation; Compliance With Statute: The provisions of subsection A of
this section notwithstanding, no penalty shall be greater than that established
by state statute for the same offense. (2009 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. 65 ILCS 5/1-2-1, 5/1-2-1.1.
1-4-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Application Of Penalty: The penalty provided in this chapter shall be
applicable to every section of this code the same as though it were a part of
each and every separate section.
   B.   Acts Punishable Under Different Sections: In all cases where the same
offense is made punishable or is created by different clauses or sections of
this code, the prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed, but not
more than one recovery shall be had against the same person for the same
offense; provided, that the revocation of a license or permit shall not be
considered a recovery or penalty so as to bar any other penalty being enforced.
   C.   Breach Of Provisions: Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to
do any act constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code and
there shall be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the
provisions of this chapter shall apply. (2009 Code)
1-4-3: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS:
No provision of this code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty, unless the intention of
the city council to impose such fine or penalty on such officer or employee is
specifically and clearly expressed in the section creating the duty. (2009
Code)
1-4-4: COLLECTION OF ATTORNEY FEES:
In furtherance of the goal of efficient enforcement of the ordinances of the
city, it is hereby provided that in any ordinance prosecution maintained by the
city in which the alleged violator is found guilty of violating any ordinance
of the city, the city shall have, in addition to any fine imposed, the payment
of its reasonable attorney fees for the maintenance of such prosecution. (Ord.,
10-5-1987)
CHAPTER 5
MAYOR
SECTION:
1-5-1: Qualifications; Term Of Office
1-5-2: Bond
1-5-3: Compensation
1-5-4: Vacancy In Office
1-5-5: General Powers And Duties
1-5-6: Duties Regarding City Officers
1-5-7: Approval, Veto Of Ordinances
1-5-8: Deputy Mayor; Temporary Chairperson
1-5-1: QUALIFICATIONS 1 ; TERM OF OFFICE:
The chief executive officer of the city shall be the mayor, who shall be a
qualified elector of the city and shall have resided within the city at least
one year next preceding the election, and who shall hold his office for four
(4) years and until his successor is elected and qualified. (1925 Code § 6-1;
amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  1-11-3 of this title.
1-5-2: BOND:
Before entering upon the duties of his office, the mayor shall execute a bond
to the city in the penal sum of three thousand dollars ($3,000.00), with such
sureties as the city council shall approve, conditioned for the faithful
performance of the duties of his office. (1925 Code § 6-2; amd. 1981 Code)
1-5-3: COMPENSATION:
The mayor of the city shall receive as compensation for his services a salary
of three thousand six hundred dollars ($3,600.00) per annum for fiscal year
2003/2004 and all subsequent years. (1925 Code § 6-11; amd. 1981 Code; Ord., 7-
6-1981; Ord., 9-2002)
1-5-4: VACANCY IN OFFICE:
If a vacancy occurs in the office of the mayor, the vacancy must be filled by
the city council electing one of their members as acting mayor. Except as set
forth in 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/3.1-10-50(d), the acting mayor shall
perform the duties and possess all the rights and powers of the mayor until a
mayor is elected at the next general municipal election and has qualified.
(1925 Code § 6-3; amd. 2009 Code)
1-5-5: GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES:
The mayor shall:
   A.   Do and perform all such duties as are enjoined upon him by the laws of
the state and the ordinances of the city, and shall take care that all the
ordinances of the city are duly enforced, respected and observed.
   B.   Preside at all meetings of the city council, but shall not vote except:
      1.   In the case of a tie;
      2.   When half of the alderman elected have voted in favor of an
ordinance, resolution or motion;
      3.   When a vote greater than a majority of the corporate authorities is
require by state statute or local ordinance to adopt an ordinance resolution,
or motion; or
      4.   As otherwise allowed or required by law.
   C.   Preserve order and decorum at all meetings.
   D.   At the first regular meeting of the city council of each fiscal year,
and from time to time thereafter, give the city council information in writing
relative to the affairs of the city, and he shall recommend for their
consideration as he may deem expedient.
   E.   In the fulfillment of such duties, devote so much of his time as a
faithful and efficient discharge thereof may require.
   F.   Decide upon all applications for licenses or reject the same, but it
shall be his duty to grant all such applications when the same are in
accordance with the laws and the ordinances of the city, and the applicant is
of lawful age, and of good moral character and is qualified according to law
and the ordinances of the city to receive the same; and the mayor shall have
power to revoke any license so granted by him for a violation of the laws or
ordinances of the city or for gross misconduct on the part of the licensee.
Provided, that the party aggrieved may appeal to the city council at its next
regular meeting when, if a majority of all the members elected to the city
council so vote, said license shall again become valid and in full force.
   G.   Sign all commissions, licenses, permits and warrants granted, issued or
drawn by the order of the city council or authorized by ordinance of the city.
He shall sign all contracts where the city is a party unless otherwise
provided, and it shall be his special duty to see that the other contracting
party faithfully complies with the contract; and in all suits where the city is
a party, he shall advise with and assist the city attorney in prosecuting or
defending the same, as the case may be. (1925 Code §§ 6-5, 6-6, and 6-10; amd.
Ord. 2020-01, 1-13-2020)
1-5-6: DUTIES REGARDING CITY OFFICERS:
   A.   The mayor shall, by and with the advice and approval of a majority of
the city council, appoint all officers of the city whose appointments are not
otherwise provided for by law; and whenever a vacancy shall occur in any office
which by law or ordinance he is empowered and required to fill, he shall, at
the next regular meeting of the city council after such vacancy, communicate to
the city council the name of his appointee to such office, and pending the
concurrence of the council in such appointment, he may designate some suitable
person to discharge the function of such office. (1925 Code § 6-7)
   B.   The mayor shall supervise the conduct of all of the officers of the
city and:
      1.   See that they faithfully and efficiently discharge the duties of
their respective offices.
      2.   Inquire into all reasonable complaints made against any officer, and
cause any violation or neglect of duty to be promptly corrected.
      3.   In case he becomes satisfied that any officer wilfully neglects or
violates his duty, cause such officer to be prosecuted and punished. (1925 Code
§ 6-8)
      4.   Have the power to remove any officer appointed by him on any written
charge if, in his opinion, the best interests of the city demand such removal,
but he shall report the reasons for such removal to the city council at a
meeting to be held not less than five (5) days nor more than ten (10) days
after such removal. If the mayor shall fail or refuse to file with the city
council a statement of the reasons for such removal or if the city council, by
a two-thirds (2/3) vote of all its members authorized by law to be elected, by
yeas and nays, to be entered upon its record, disapproves of such removal, such
officer shall thereupon become restored to the office from which he was
removed, but he shall give new bond and take a new oath of office. No officer
shall be removed a second time for the same offense. (1925 Code § 6-8; amd.
2009 Code)
1-5-7: APPROVAL, VETO OF ORDINANCES:
The mayor shall carefully inspect all ordinances passed by the city council and
affix his official signature to such as he may approve and return them to the
city clerk within ten (10) days after their passage. All ordinances passed as
aforesaid which do not meet his approval, he shall return to the city council
with his objection thereto in writing at the next regular meeting of the
council occurring not less than five (5) days after the passage thereof. Such
veto may extend to any one or more items or appropriations contained in any
ordinance making an appropriation or to the entire ordinance; and in case the
veto only extends to one or more items of appropriation of such ordinance, the
residue thereof shall take effect and be in force. In case the mayor shall fail
to return any ordinance, with his objections thereto, by the time aforesaid, he
shall be deemed to have approved such ordinance and the same shall take effect
accordingly. (1925 Code § 6-9; amd. 2009 Code)
1-5-8: DEPUTY MAYOR; TEMPORARY CHAIRPERSON:
   A.   Only those serving as a duly elected or appointed alderperson of the
City of Virginia shall be eligible for appointment to the position of deputy
mayor.
   B.   The deputy mayor shall perform the duties and possess all of the rights
and powers of the mayor, consistent with the rights and duties set forth in 65
ILCS 5/3.1-35-35(a), when the mayor is absent from the city, is under
disability and thus incapable of acting as mayor, or when the position of mayor
is vacant as defined by the Illinois Municipal Code. The mayor shall be deemed
absent or incapable of acting as mayor when so declared by such mayor or when
so designated by the mayor's personal attending physician. A notice of absence
or incapacity shall be in writing and signed either by the mayor or the mayor's
personal attending physician and delivered to city hall to be filed with the
city's official records.
   C.   When acting in the capacity of mayor, the deputy mayor shall not be
entitled to vote in both capacities as mayor and as alderperson, consistent
with 65 ILCS 5/3.1-35-35(a).
   D.   The deputy mayor shall receive no additional compensation while acting
in the capacity of mayor.
   E.   At times when the deputy mayor is not acting in the capacity of mayor,
the deputy mayor shall perform the duties and possess all of the rights and
powers of an alderperson.
   F.   In the event that both the deputy mayor and mayor are absent or
incapacitated as defined herein, the corporate authorities may elect one of
their members to act as a temporary chairman consistent with 65 ILCS 5/3.1-35-
35(b). Written notice of absence or incapacity of the deputy mayor for the
purpose of this subsection F shall be provided in the same manner as set forth
in subsection B above. A temporary chairman shall have only the powers of a
presiding officer and a right to vote only in the capacity as alderperson or
trustee on any ordinance, resolution, or motion.
   G.   A temporary chairperson shall receive no additional compensation while
acting as temporary chairperson.
   H.   In the event both the positions of mayor and deputy mayor are vacant,
as defined by the Illinois Municipal Code, the corporate authorities may elect
a mayor pro tern consistent with 65 ILCS 5/3.1-35-35(a). (Ord. 2025-6, 6-9-
2025)
CHAPTER 6
CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-6-1: Composition; Powers; Vacancy
1-6-2: Qualifications
1-6-3: Term Of Office
1-6-4: Meetings
1-6-5: Voting Requirements
1-6-6: Signature On Bonds Prohibited
1-6-7: Compensation
1-6-8: Standing Committees
1-6-9: Special Committees
1-6-1: COMPOSITION; POWERS; VACANCY:
The city council shall consist of the mayor and two (2) aldermen from each
ward. The city council shall be the judge of the election and qualification of
its own members and exercise the powers conferred upon it by the laws of the
state and the ordinances of the city. If a vacancy shall occur in the office of
alderman, the vacancy must be filled by the mayor or acting mayor in accordance
with 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/3.1-10-50(e). (1925 Code § 10-1; amd. 2009
Code)
1-6-2: QUALIFICATIONS 1 :
No person shall be eligible to the office of alderman if:
   A.   He is not a qualified elector and does not reside within the ward from
which he is elected.
   B.   He is in arrears in the payment of any tax or other liability due the
city.
   C.   He is directly or indirectly interested in any contract whatever to
which the city is a party. There shall be compliance with 65 Illinois Compiled
Statutes 5/3.1-55-10 regarding interests in contracts 2 .
   D.   He shall have been convicted of malfeasance, bribery or other corrupt
practices or crimes.
   E.   At the same time as he serves, he holds any other office under the city
government. (1925 Code § 10-2; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  1-11-3 of this title.
2 2. See also section
  1-11-6 of this title.
1-6-3: TERM OF OFFICE:
Each alderman shall hold his office for the term of four (4) years and until
his successor is elected and qualified. (1925 Code § 10-2; amd. 1981 Code)
1-6-4: MEETINGS:
   A.   Regular Meetings: The regular meetings of the city council shall be
held in the city hall or such other place as the city council shall desire on
the second Monday of each and every month at seven o’clock (7:00) P.M.
Adjourned meetings may be held for the purpose of completing the unfinished
business of the regular meeting at such time or times to which the regular
meeting is adjourned. (Ord., 12-2-2002; amd. Ord. 2025-5, 5-12-2025)
   B.   Special Meetings: Special meetings may be called by the mayor or any
three (3) aldermen when, in their discretion, they may deem it necessary, in
which event, the meeting shall be called in the following manner: The mayor, or
three (3) aldermen, as the case may be, shall file in the city clerk's office a
statement in writing setting forth the object and purpose of such special
meeting and directing the clerk to give notice of the same. Thereupon, the
clerk shall cause to be served personally upon each member of the council or
left at his usual place of business a notice of such special meeting, setting
forth the object and purpose thereof and the time of holding the same. No
business other than that mentioned in the call shall be transacted at such
special meeting. (1925 Code § 10-4)
   C.   Open And Closed Meetings: All meetings shall be open to the public
except for those closed meetings authorized by 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes
120/2(c). (2009 Code)
   D.   Order Of Business: The city council may, by resolution, duly adopt and
enter of record their proceedings and pass such rules pertaining to the order
of business and mode of procedure in transacting business as they may, from
time to time, see fit. (1925 Code § 10-6)
   E.   Electronic Attendance At Meetings: Any member of the public body,
including the Mayor, may attend any meeting of a public body as defined in the
Open Meetings Act via electronic means, provided that there is compliance with
the rules for such attendance as set forth in subsection F of this section. The
terms "electronic means" and "electronically" are defined to mean by video or
audio conferencing.
   F.   Rules For Attendance By Electronic Means:
      1.   Qualifications: A member of the City Council, including the Mayor,
may attend a meeting electronically if the member meets the following
conditions:
         a.   The member must notify the Clerk at least twenty four (24) hours
before the meeting, unless impractical (such as in the case of the sudden onset
of an illness or an emergency), so that necessary communications equipment can
be arranged. Failure to make the necessary technical arrangements will result
in denial of a request for remote attendance.
         b.   The member must assert one of the following reasons why he or she
is unable to attend the meeting in person:
            (1)   The member cannot attend because of personal illness or
disability; or
            (2)   The member cannot attend because of his or her employment
obligations or because the member is attending to the business of the City of
Virginia; or
            (3)   The member cannot attend because of a family or other
emergency.
      2.   Authorization To Participate:
         a.   The Clerk, after receiving the electronic attendance request,
shall inform the Mayor and City Council of the request for electronic
attendance.
         b.   After establishing that a quorum is otherwise physically present
at a meeting where an Alderman or Mayor desires to attend electronically, the
presiding officer shall state that: 1) a notice was received by a member of the
City Council or Mayor in accordance with these rules, and 2) the member will be
deemed authorized to attend the meeting electronically unless a motion
objecting to the member's electronic attendance is made, seconded, and approved
by two-thirds (2/3) of the members of the City Council physically present at
the meeting. If no such motion is made and seconded or if any such motion fails
to achieve the required vote by the members of the City Council physically
present at the meeting, then the request by the member to attend the meeting
electronically shall be deemed approved by the City Council and the presiding
officer shall declare the requesting member present. After such declaration by
the presiding officer, the question of a member's electronic attendance may not
be reconsidered.
      3.   Adequate Equipment Required: The member participating electronically
and other members of the City Council must be able to communicate effectively,
and members of the audience must be able to hear all communications at the
meeting site. Before allowing electronic attendance at any meeting, the City
Clerk shall provide equipment adequate to accomplish this objective at the
meeting site.
      4.   Minutes: Any member attending electronically shall be considered an
off-site attendee and counted as present electronically for that meeting if the
member is allowed to attend. The meeting minutes shall also reflect and state
specifically whether each member is physically present or present by electronic
means.
      5.   Rights Of Remote Member: A member permitted to attend electronically
will be able to express his or her comments during the meeting and participate
in the same capacity as those members physically present, subject to all
general meeting guidelines and procedures previously adopted and adhered to.
The member attending electronically shall be heard, considered, and counted as
to any vote taken. Accordingly, the name of any member attending electronically
shall be called during any vote taken, and his or her vote counted and recorded
by the Clerk and placed in the minutes for the corresponding meeting. A member
attending electronically may leave a meeting and return as in the case of any
member, provided the member attending electronically shall announce his or her
leaving and returning.
      6.   Committees, Boards And Commissions: These rules shall apply to all
committees, boards and commissions established by authority of this Code and/or
City Council. (Ord. 2017-07, 11-24-2017)
1-6-5: VOTING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Members Required To Vote; Prohibited Voting: No member shall vote on
any question in which he is directly and personally interested. On all other
questions which may be brought before the Council for action, every member
shall vote unless such member be excused by the Mayor. (1925 Code § 10-7)
   B.   Yeas And Nays Required: The yeas and nays shall be taken upon the
passage of all ordinances and on propositions to create any liability against
the City, or for the expenditure or appropriation of its money, and in all
other cases, at the request of any member, which request shall be entered on
the journal of its proceedings. The concurrence of a majority of all the
members elect in the City Council shall be necessary to the passage of any such
ordinance or proposition; provided, it shall require a two-thirds (2/3) vote of
all the Aldermen elect to sell any City property. (1925 Code § 10-8)
   C.   Reconsideration: No vote of the City Council shall be reconsidered or
rescinded at a special meeting, unless at such special meeting, there shall be
present as many Aldermen as when such vote was taken. (1925 Code § 10-9)
1-6-6: SIGNATURE ON BONDS PROHIBITED:
No member of the Council shall sign any bond in any case wherein the City is
interested. (1925 Code § 10-2; amd. 1981 Code)
1-6-7: COMPENSATION:
Aldermen shall receive one thousand two hundred dollars ($1,200.00) per annum
for the fiscal year 2003/2004 and all subsequent years. (Ord., 9-2002; amd.
2009 Code)
1-6-8: STANDING COMMITTEES:
   A.   General Provisions:
      1.   Committees Established: It shall be the duty of the Mayor, at the
regular meeting of the City Council in May of each year, or as soon thereafter
as may be, and in the case of a newly established committee, as soon as
practical after passage of an ordinance establishing said committee and then in
May of each year thereafter, or as soon thereafter as may be, to appoint the
following standing committees of the City Council: (Ord. 12-05, 3-12-2012)
   Finance Committee
   Ordinance Committee
   Water and Sewer Committee
   Streets, Alleys and Lights Committee
   Buildings Committee
   Police Committee
      TIF Committee
(1925 Code § 11-1; amd. 1981 Code; Ord. 12-05, 3-12-2012)
      2.   Composition; Chair: With the exception of the TIF Committee, which
hereafter will be provided for, the committees appointed under this section
shall, in each case, consist of three (3) Aldermen. The Mayor shall be ex
officio member of every committee whose appointment is provided for in the
ordinances of the City and shall have the privilege of receiving notice and
being present at the meetings of all committees, but shall have no right to
vote on any question before said committees unless the vote on a particular
matter results in a tie, whereupon, the Mayor shall cast the deciding vote. In
each instance, the Alderman first named in order of appointment shall be the
Chair of his respective committee and preside over its deliberations, but as
such Chair, he shall not be deprived of his vote on any subject, and unless
excused by the committee, he shall be compelled to cast his vote. The TIF
Committee shall consist of one Alderman, City Treasurer, and four (4) citizens,
all of which shall be appointed by the Mayor to said committee as established
herein. (Ord., 10-2-1995; amd. Ord. 12-05, 3-12-2012)
      3.   Duties Generally: Notwithstanding any of the provisions with
reference to any standing committee of the City as hereinafter set out, the
said standing committees of the City shall not be limited in their action
thereby, but they shall at all times and in all manner exercise all of the
necessary duties that may pertain to their respective committees, anything in
said provisions to the contrary notwithstanding, but it shall be the duty of
the said standing committees to keep a close watch on the affairs of the City
government. Each committee shall promptly and thoroughly investigate all
matters which may be referred to it and report thereon in writing at its
earliest opportunity and do and perform all other duties as the City Council
may from time to time prescribe by resolution, motion or otherwise. (1925 Code
§ 11-13)
      4.   Reports: Any report of a committee of the City Council shall be
deferred for final action thereon to the next regular meeting of the same,
after the report is made upon the request of any two (2) Aldermen upon any
subject referred to it, shall report in writing and shall attach to their
report all papers or documents in the possession of the committee relative to
the matters so referred. (1925 Code § 11-14)
   B.   Committee On Finance:
      1.   The Committee On Finance of the City Council shall from time to time
examine the books, accounts and reports of the City officers and see if they
are regularly and accurately kept and preserved, and that the books and papers
belonging to the various departments and offices are secure from loss by fire
or otherwise. The committee shall report to the City Council any neglect or
failure of any officer to keep and maintain his books and accounts properly and
to preserve the papers pertaining to his office.
      2.   The Finance Committee shall, at the close of each fiscal year and at
such other times as the City Council may direct, examine and compare the
reports and accounts of all the City officers that may in any way relate to the
finances of the City, and shall report thereon to the City Council.
      3.   The Committee On Finance shall, each year during the months within
which said report may be required by law, prepare a budget and then make an
estimate of the probable receipts and expenditures for Municipal purposes for
the ensuing year, and make a table of appropriations to be recommended to the
City Council.
      4.   The Committee On Finance shall see to the borrowing of money,
issuing of bonds, and preparation of ordinances for the appropriation and levy
of taxes. The committee shall make arrangements for the payment of debts
maturing against the City and shall be charged with all matters pertaining to
the finances of the City. (1925 Code § 11-4; amd. 1981 Code)
   C.   Committee On Ordinances: The Committee On Ordinances shall have a
general supervision of the preparation and revision of the ordinances of the
City. The committee shall, from time to time, report to the City Council such
ordinances as the committee deems advisable to be passed, and the committee
shall at all times assist the City Attorney in the preparation of the
ordinances required by the City Council. (1925 Code § 11-6)
   D.   Committee On Water And Sewer: The Committee On Water and Sewer shall
exercise general supervision of all sewers and drains within the City. The
committee shall see that the same are kept in good repair and in sanitary
condition and shall have the power to condemn any sewer as in the committee's
judgment should be condemned and make such reports as may be deemed necessary
to keep the sewer system of the City in proper working condition. The committee
shall, from time to time, recommend to the City Council such additional sewers
or systems of sewers that, in the committee's judgment, should be installed, or
the enlarging of such sewers as the growth of the City has rendered necessary.
(1925 Code § 11-10; amd. 1981 Code)
   E.   Committee On Streets, Alleys And Lights: The Committee On Streets,
Alleys and Lights shall have the general supervision of the streets, alleys and
sidewalks in the City. The committee shall take such steps as it deems
necessary to keep the streets, alleys and sidewalks of the City in a good,
passable and safe condition. The committee shall give directions from time to
time to the Public Works Director who shall follow the instructions so given.
The committee shall report to the City Council from time to time when, in its
opinion, it may deem necessary, such changes, repairs and improvements upon the
streets of the City, but no improvements shall be made upon the streets or
alleys, excepting ordinary and necessary repairs, until the City Council has
ordered the same upon the recommendation of the committee. The committee shall
see that all sidewalks are kept in good repair and in a passable condition, and
shall, from time to time, with the concurrence of the City Council, order such
improvements to be made and repairs performed upon the sidewalks as in its
opinion may be requisite or necessary. The committee shall have the power to
order old walks condemned and ordinary walks altered in accordance with the
requirements of the City Council and the ordinances of the City. The committee
may prepare a standard of grades and file a report thereof in the Office of the
City Clerk. (1925 Code § 11-11; amd. 1981 Code)
   F.   Committee On Buildings: The Committee On Buildings shall have the
general supervision of buildings. The committee shall supervise the maintenance
and repair of City buildings, and seek bids for each additional construction of
buildings for the City.
   G.   Committee On Police: The Committee On Police shall have general
supervision of the Police Department of the City. The committee shall recommend
to the Council its recommendations for the Police Department. (1981 Code)
   H.   Committee On TIF: The Committee On TIF shall have general supervision
of the City TIF program. Additionally, this committee shall review requests for
reimbursement related to any TIF redevelopment agreement and make
recommendations to the City Council which bills are eligible for reimbursement
and should be paid from the appropriate TIF account. The committee shall also
review redevelopment plans submitted to the City and make recommendations to
the City Council on the funding of redevelopment projects. The committee shall
also be charged with such other duties as necessary for the implementation and
administration of the TIF program and take action thereon with City Council
approval. (Ord. 12-05, 3-12-2012)
1-6-9: SPECIAL COMMITTEES:
Whenever a matter is presented to the City Council, the subject matter of which
does not come under the control of any of the regular committees appointed
under this chapter or which embraces more than one subject under the
supervision of two (2) or more committees of the City Council, or whenever a
matter is presented of such importance as to require special attention, the
Mayor may appoint a special committee, consisting of as many members of the
City Council as he deems advisable, to which said matter may be referred, with
such directions as the Council shall deem proper, and whenever any special
committee is so appointed, said committee shall be governed by the same rules
and make report in the same manner as the regular committees of the City
Council, unless otherwise instructed. (1925 Code § 11-15)
CHAPTER 7
CITY CLERK
SECTION:
1-7-1: Oath And Bond
1-7-2: Powers And Duties
1-7-3: City Revenues
1-7-4: Compensation
1-7-1: OATH AND BOND:
Before entering upon the duties of his office, the city clerk shall take the
oath prescribed for other city officers and shall execute a bond to the city in
the penal sum of ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00), with such sureties as may
be approved by the city council, conditioned for the faithful performance of
the duties of his office and the payment of all monies that may be received by
him according to law and the ordinances of the city, which monies shall be
filed with the city treasurer. (1925 Code § 7-1; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
1-7-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Custodian Of Seal And Documents: The city clerk shall keep the
corporate seal, to be provided by the city council, and all papers belonging to
the city.
   B.   Attend Council Meetings: The city clerk shall attend all meetings of
the city council and keep a full and complete record of its proceedings in a
suitable book to be styled "Record Of City Council", and copies of all papers
duly filed in his office and transcripts from the journals and other records
and files of his office, certified by him under the corporate seal, shall be
evidence in all courts in like manner as if the originals were produced.
   C.   Issue Notices Of Meetings: The city clerk shall issue and cause to be
served upon all aldermen notices of all special meetings of the city council,
also notices to the members of the different committees of that body and all
other persons whose attendance may be required before any such committee when
so directed by the chair thereof. (1925 Code § 7-3)
   D.   Deliver Reports And Communications: Upon adjournment of each meeting of
the city council, the city clerk shall, without delay, deliver to the several
committees of that body and to the officers of the city all petitions and
communications, reports, resolutions, orders, claims and other papers referred
to such committees or officers by the city council. He shall also, without
delay, deliver to the mayor all ordinances or resolutions in his charge which
may require the approval or other action by the mayor. (1925 Code § 7-5)
   E.   Record And Publish Ordinances: The city clerk shall record and properly
index in a book kept for that purpose all ordinances passed by the city
council, and at the foot of the record of each ordinance so recorded, he shall
make a memorandum of the date of passage and of the time and manner of
publication of such ordinance, which record and memorandum, or certified copy
thereof, shall be prima facie evidence of the passage and legal publication of
such ordinance for all purposes whatsoever. He shall cause all ordinances
imposing any fine, penalty, imprisonment or forfeiture, or making any
appropriation, to be published within thirty (30) days after its passage in a
newspaper of general circulation in the city, and he shall file and preserve in
his office one or more copies of the newspaper containing ordinances so
published. (1925 Code § 7-7; amd. 2009 Code)
   F.   Prepare Official Papers: The city clerk shall prepare all commissions,
licenses, permits or other official documents required to be issued by him
under the laws and ordinances of the city, and shall attest the same with the
city seal, and he shall in a like manner attest all deeds for the sale of real
estate owned and conveyed by the city. He shall furnish certified copies of any
ordinance, bond or other papers in his keeping to any city officer when so
required. (1925 Code § 7-8)
   G.   Records Kept; Deliver To Successor: The city clerk shall have the
charge, custody and control of all deeds, leases, warrants, contracts, bonds,
obligations, vouchers, books, records, maps and papers of every kind belonging
to the city, the custody of which is not herein given to another officer, and
upon the expiration of his official term, he shall deliver all of such books,
records, papers and effects to his successor in office. (1925 Code § 7-11)
   H.   Furnish Report Forms: The city clerk shall provide and constantly keep
on hand and furnish on request, without charge, to any person required by law
or ordinance to make reports to the city, all blanks necessary for such
reports. (1925 Code § 7-13)
   I.   Attest Licenses; Record Kept: The city clerk shall attest all licenses
granted by the mayor or city council and shall keep a register of the same,
showing the date of issue, time of expiration, business licenses and amount
paid. (1925 Code § 7-14)
   J.   Monthly Reports: It shall be the duty of the city clerk to make a
report to the city council at the regular meeting each month of the exact
condition of each fund or appropriation, the total amount which has been used
or expended thereof, the balance, if any, which is subject to be drawn upon,
and whenever any fund or appropriation is exhausted, the clerk shall, without
delay, so notify the city council, and he shall not thereafter draw any warrant
against such fund or appropriation until the same shall be renewed. (1925 Code
§ 7-15; amd. 2009 Code)
   K.   Additional Duties: In addition to the foregoing duties, the city clerk
shall perform all such other and further duties pertaining to his office as are
or may be imposed by ordinance or resolution of the city council. (1925 Code §
7-16)
1-7-3: CITY REVENUES:
   A.   General Supervision; Report Of Estimates: The city clerk shall exercise
a general supervision over all the officers of the city charged in any manner
with the receipt, collection or disbursement of corporation revenues and the
collection and return of all revenues into the treasury. He shall, on or before
May 15 in each year, and before the annual appropriations are made by the city
council, submit to the city council a report of his estimates, as nearly as may
be, of monies necessary to defray the expenses of the corporation during the
current fiscal year. He shall, in said report, class the different objects and
branches of expenditures, giving as nearly as may be, the amount required for
each; and for the purpose of making such report, he is authorized to require of
all officers their statement of the condition and expenses of their respective
offices or departments, with any proposed improvements and the probable expense
thereof, all contracts made and unfinished, and amount of any and all
unexpended appropriations of the preceding fiscal year. He shall, in such
report, show the aggregate income of liabilities outstanding upon which
interest is to be paid, the bonds and debts due and payable during the year,
when due and when payable, and in such report, he shall give such other
information to the city council as he may deem necessary to the end that the
city council may duly understand the money exigencies and the demands upon the
city for the current year. (1925 Code § 7-4)
   B.   Warrants: The city clerk shall draw all warrants on the city treasurer
for claims allowed by the city council and shall keep in a suitable book an
accurate list of all warrants drawn, showing the name of the person in whose
name drawn, the date, number and amount of each, and he shall take the receipt
of every person for the warrant drawn, upon the delivery thereof. All warrants
drawn upon the city treasurer shall be signed by the mayor and countersigned by
the clerk and shall specify therein the particular fund or appropriation to
which the same is chargeable and the person to whom payable, and no money shall
be paid otherwise than upon such warrants so drawn. The clerk shall preserve
all warrants returned to him. (1925 Code § 7-6)
   C.   Accounts Of Revenues; Record Of Bonds: The city clerk shall open and
keep in a neat methodical manner a set of books in which shall be kept a
detailed account of the city revenues and of each separate fund, crediting the
same with all receipts or appropriations and charging it with all warrants
drawn thereon. He shall keep an accurate account of all debts due from or owing
the city and shall keep, in a book or books kept expressly for that purpose, an
accurate list of all outstanding bonds of the city, showing the number and
amount of each, and for and to whom said bonds were issued. When any city bonds
are purchased or paid or canceled, said book or books shall show the fact, and
in his annual report, he shall describe particularly the bonds sold during the
year and the terms of sale, with each item of expense thereof. He shall also
keep a list of all notices and other obligations given by or payable to the
city and shall show the date, the person to or by whom payable and such other
particulars as shall be necessary to a full understanding thereof. Such books
and all other instruments kept in the clerk's office shall be subject to the
examination of the mayor and the members of the city council. (1925 Code § 7-
12)
1-7-4: COMPENSATION:
The city clerk shall receive, as compensation for his services, a salary of one
thousand eight hundred dollars ($1,800.00) per annum for the fiscal year 2003/
2004 and all subsequent years, payable monthly at the end of each month. (1925
Code § 7-16; amd. 1981 Code; Ord., 9-2002)
CHAPTER 8
CITY ATTORNEY
SECTION:
1-8-1: Qualifications; Appointment
1-8-2: Powers And Duties
1-8-3: Compensation
1-8-1: QUALIFICATIONS; APPOINTMENT:
To be eligible to the office of city attorney, a person must be regularly
licensed to practice law in the courts of the state. The city attorney shall be
appointed by the mayor, with the concurrence of the city council. (1925 Code §
8-1; amd. 1981 Code)
1-8-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Draft Documents; Legal Advice: The city attorney shall draw such
ordinances, deeds, leases, contracts and other papers as shall be required of
him by the mayor, city council or any committee thereof. He shall examine all
instruments pertaining to the interests of the city submitted to him by the
mayor, city council or any committee thereof and pass on the legality of the
same. He shall, when required, advise the mayor, city council or any city
officer in all matters of law in which the interests of the city are involved,
and shall, when required, furnish written opinions when requested by the mayor
or city council. (1925 Code § 8-2)
   B.   Prosecute And Defend Suits: The city attorney is charged with the
prosecution of all action for violations of the ordinances of the city and with
the conducting of all proceedings before a court of record and all actions in
which the city is a party in any of the courts of record in the county, or upon
appeal taken from any court of record. He shall institute and prosecute all
actions in every case where there has been a violation of any city ordinance
when instructed so to do by the mayor, city council or any committee thereof,
or upon the complaint of any person claiming, in his judgment, the public
interest requests that the same shall be prosecuted. He shall defend, on behalf
of the city, all cases wherein the interest of the city is involved. No plea of
guilty for the violation of any ordinance shall be received before the court of
record unless the city attorney, or his regularly consulted assistant, is
present or has been previously notified of the pendency of the proceeding and
the time set for hearing. Said notice shall be served by the chief of police or
other officer attending on said court. (1925 Code § 8-3; amd. 1981 Code)
   C.   Collect Judgments: The city attorney shall collect all judgments
recovered in favor of the city and shall cause execution to be issued thereon.
In all cases wherein judgments are rendered against the city, he shall examine
all fee bills and certify to their correctness and the liability of the city
therefor. (1925 Code § 8-4)
   D.   Keep Records; Deliver To Successor:
      1.   The city attorney shall keep, in a proper book to be provided for
that purpose, a register of all actions in courts of record prosecuted or
defended by him in which the city may be a party and all proceedings had
therein, and also a record of all written opinions furnished by him to the
city, which said record shall be open to the inspection of the mayor, the city
clerk or any member of the city council. (1925 Code § 8-7)
      2.   Upon the expiration of his term of office, or resignation or removal
therefrom, the city attorney shall forthwith turn over to his successor in
office all books, papers or other instruments in his hands belonging to the
city, together with a statement in writing showing what action if any has been
taken in any action then pending, wherein the city is a party, and giving such
information as he may possess with respect to evidence or witnesses in such
action or actions. (1925 Code § 8-8)
1-8-3: COMPENSATION:
The city attorney shall receive as compensation such sums as shall be
determined by the city council. (Ord., 10-2-1995)
CHAPTER 9
CITY TREASURER
SECTION:
1-9-1: Oath And Bond
1-9-2: Private Use Of City Funds
1-9-3: Report Delinquent Officers
1-9-4: Special Assessment Funds
1-9-5: General Financial Procedures
1-9-6: Reports Required
1-9-7: Compensation
1-9-1: OATH AND BOND:
Before entering upon the duties of his office, the city treasurer shall take
the oath prescribed for city officers and shall execute a bond, with securities
to be approved by the city council, in the penal sum of ten thousand dollars
($10,000.00), with not less than two (2) good and sufficient sureties,
conditioned for the faithful performance of his office and the payment of all
monies received by him according to law and the ordinances of the city. The
premium on said bond shall be paid by the city. (1925 Code § 9-1; amd. 1981
Code; 2009 Code)
1-9-2: PRIVATE USE OF CITY FUNDS:
The city treasurer shall keep all monies belonging to the city, and in his
hands, separate and distinct from his own monies, and he is hereby expressly
prohibited from using, either directly or indirectly, city monies or warrants
in his custody and keeping for his own use and benefit, or that of any other
person or persons whomsoever. Any violation of this section shall subject the
treasurer to immediate removal from office by the city council, who shall, when
such conversion of funds is brought to the knowledge thereof, by satisfactory
evidence, declare the office vacant. (1925 Code § 9-3)
1-9-3: REPORT DELINQUENT OFFICERS:
The city treasurer shall report to the city clerk any officer authorized to
receive money who may fail to make return of the monies received by him at the
time required by law and the ordinances of the city. (1925 Code § 9-5)
1-9-4: SPECIAL ASSESSMENT FUNDS:
All monies received on any special assessment shall be held by the city
treasurer as a special fund to be applied to the payment of the improvement for
which the assessment was made, and said monies shall be used for no other
purpose whatever unless to reimburse the city for monies expended for such
improvement. (1925 Code § 9-4)
1-9-5: GENERAL FINANCIAL PROCEDURES:
The city treasurer shall receive all monies belonging to the city and shall
keep books of account in such a manner as to show with entire accuracy all
monies received by him, and from whom and on what account they shall have been
received, and of all monies paid out by him and on what account they shall have
been paid, and shall keep a separate account of each fund or appropriation, and
debits and credits belonging thereto, in such a way that said books and
accounts will exhibit at all times the true financial condition of the city,
and in such a manner that said books may be readily understood and
investigated. He shall give every person paying money into the treasury a
receipt therefor, specifying the date of payment and upon what account paid,
and he shall file copies of such receipts with the city clerk at the date of
his monthly report, which books and papers and files of said office shall at
all times be open to the examination of the mayor, the city clerk, the finance
committee or any member of the city council. (1925 Code § 9-2)
1-9-6: REPORTS REQUIRED:
   A.   Monthly Statements: The city treasurer shall, at the regular meeting
each month, render an account to the city council, under oath, showing the
state of the treasury at the date of such account and the balance of money in
the treasury. He shall accompany such accounts with a statement of all monies
received in the treasury and upon what account, together with all warrants
redeemed and paid by him, which said warrants, with any and all vouchers held
by him, shall be delivered to the city clerk and filed with his said account in
the clerk's office upon the date of such settlement. He shall return all
warrants paid by him stamped "Paid". He shall keep an accurate register of all
warrants redeemed and paid by him, showing the number, date and amount of each,
the fund from which paid and the name of the person to whom and when paid, and
shall cancel all warrants as soon as redeemed by him. (1925 Code § 9-6; amd.
2009 Code)
   B.   Annual Report; Publication: The city treasurer shall annually, within
six (6) months after the end of the fiscal year, make out and file with the
city clerk a full and detailed account of all receipts and expenditures of the
city and all his transactions as such city treasurer during the preceding
fiscal year, which said statement shall exhibit under separate and appropriate
headings the several accounts with the several funds or appropriations. It
shall be the duty of the city clerk to submit his counter annual financial
report, together with the report of the treasurer aforesaid, to the mayor and
the committee on finance of the city council, and if the mayor and the
committee shall be satisfied that the treasurer's report properly exhibits the
true financial condition of the city, they shall return the same to the city
clerk who shall immediately cause such report to be published in a newspaper of
general circulation in the city. (1925 Code § 9-7; amd. 2009 Code)
1-9-7: COMPENSATION:
The city treasurer shall receive as compensation for his or her services one
thousand eight hundred dollars ($1,800.00) per annum for fiscal year 2003/2004
and all subsequent years. The city treasurer shall receive no other
compensation by reason of his office. Said compensation shall be paid
quarterly. (Ord., 2-8-1985; amd. Ord., 9-2002)
CHAPTER 10
PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR
SECTION:
1-10-1: Office Created; Appointment; Removal
1-10-2: Oath Of Office
1-10-3: Records Kept
1-10-4: Compensation
1-10-1: OFFICE CREATED; APPOINTMENT; REMOVAL:
There is hereby created the office of public works director. The public works
director shall be appointed by the mayor, by and with the advice and consent of
the city council, at the first meeting of the city council after the beginning
of each municipal year or as soon thereafter as may be, and he shall hold
office during the municipal year in which he was appointed; provided, however,
the public works director shall be subject to removal from office at any time
by a majority of the city council. (2009 Code)
1-10-2: OATH OF OFFICE:
Upon entering upon the duties of his office, the public works director shall
take the oath prescribed for city officers. (1925 Code §§ 16-1, 16-8; amd. 1981
Code)
1-10-3: RECORDS KEPT:
The public works director shall keep a correct list of all implements,
materials and other property belonging to the city in his charge and
possession, and upon the expiration of his term of office or his resignation
thereof or removal therefrom, he shall turn over the same to his successor in
office. (1925 Code § 16-6; amd. 2009 Code)
1-10-4: COMPENSATION:
The public works director shall receive as compensation such sums as shall be
determined by the city council, to be paid in semimonthly installments, in lieu
of all other compensation, prerequisite or benefit in any form whatever. (1925
Code § 16-9; amd. 1981 Code)
CHAPTER 11
CITY OFFICERS AND PERSONNEL
SECTION:
1-11-1: Elective Officers; Term
1-11-2: Appointive Officers
1-11-3: Qualifications
1-11-4: Oath And Bond
1-11-5: Commission Of Officers
1-11-6: Conditions Of Office
1-11-7: Property To Successors
1-11-8: Pension Systems
1-11-9: Holidays
1-11-10: Travel, Meal And Lodging Expenses
1-11-1: ELECTIVE OFFICERS; TERM:
There shall be elected at the general election for City officers in the year
1923 and every four (4) years thereafter a Mayor, City Clerk, City Treasurer
and one (1) Alderman in each of the three (3) wards in the City, for a term of
four (4) years and until their successors shall be elected and qualified. (1925
Code § 5-1; amd. 1981 Code)
1-11-2: APPOINTIVE OFFICERS:
   A.   Created: There are hereby created the following appointive offices of
the City:
City Attorney
Chief of Police
Public Works Director
Deputy Mayor
and as many assistants for any of said offices as the City Council shall, by
resolution, determine are necessary. Said appointive officers shall hold their
offices for a term of one (1) year or until their successors are appointed and
qualify. (Ord., 10-2-1995; amd. 2009 Code)
   B.   Appointment And Approval: The Mayor shall, at the regular meeting of
the City Council in the month of May in each year, after the general election
for City officers has been had, submit to the City Council names of the
appointive officers enumerated in subsection A of this section for the
succeeding year, whereupon the City Council shall proceed by an aye and nay
vote to approve or disapprove such appointments, and no officer shall be
commissioned or permitted to serve as said officer whose appointment has not
received the approval of a majority vote of the members of the City Council. If
the City Council shall fail to approve the name of any person submitted by the
Mayor, the Mayor shall submit another name for said office, and if such name
fails to receive the approval of the Council, he shall, at each succeeding
Council meeting, submit other names for the approval of the Council. (1925 Code
§ 5-3; amd. 2009 Code; Ord. 2025-6, 6-9- 2025)
1-11-3: QUALIFICATIONS:
No person shall be eligible to any elective office of the City who is not
qualified as provided in 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/3.1-10-5. (Ord., 8-14-
2000; amd. 2009 Code)
1-11-4: OATH AND BOND:
   A.   Oath Of Office: All officers of the City, whether elected or appointed,
shall, before entering upon the duties of their respective office, take and
subscribe the following oath or affirmation:
I do solemnly swear that I will support the Constitution of the United States
and the Constitution of the State of Illinois, and that I will faithfully
discharge the duties of the office of                 , according to the best
of my ability. B. Bond Requirements: All officers, except Aldermen, shall,
before entering upon the duties of their respective offices, execute a bond
payable to the City and conditioned for the faithful performance of the duties
of the office, and the payment of all monies received by said officer,
according to law and the ordinances of the City.C. Oath And Bond Filed: Said
oath or affirmation so subscribed and bond so executed shall be filed in the
Office of the City Clerk, except the bond of the Clerk, which shall be filed
with the City Treasurer. (1925 Code § 5-7)
1-11-5: COMMISSION OF OFFICERS:
   A.   All the officers of the city, whether elected or appointed, shall be
commissioned by warrant under the corporate seal of the city, which said
commission shall be signed by the mayor and attested by the city clerk, or in
case of absence or inability of the mayor or clerk to act, then by the person
acting as presiding officer of the city council and the person serving in the
capacity of clerk; except, that the commission of the mayor shall be signed by
the clerk who shall cause the official seal to be affixed thereto, and the
commission of the clerk shall be signed by the mayor who shall cause the
official seal to be affixed thereto.B. The commission for the elective officers
shall be as follows:

1-11-6: CONDITIONS OF OFFICE:
   A.   Interest In City Contracts: No officer shall be directly or indirectly
financially interested in any contract, work or business of the city, or the
sale of any article, the expense, price or consideration of which is paid from
the treasury, or by any assessment levied by any act or ordinance, nor in the
purchase of any property that: 1) belongs to the city; 2) is sold for taxes and
assessments; or 3) is sold by virtue of legal process at the suit of the city.
There shall be compliance with 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/3.1-55-10. (1925
Code § 5-5; amd. 2009 Code)B. Hold Other City Office: No Mayor, Alderman, City
Clerk or City Treasurer shall hold any other office under the City government
during the term of his office. (1925 Code § 5-6)
1-11-7: PROPERTY TO SUCCESSORS:
Any person having been an officer of the City shall, within five (5) days after
written notification and request, deliver to his successor in office all
property, books and effects of every description in his possession belonging to
the City or appertaining to his office. (1925 Code § 5-9; amd. 2009 Code)
1-11-8: PENSION SYSTEMS:
   A.   City To Provide: The City Council, as it may from time to time
determine to be in the best interests of the City, may provide for pensions,
individual retirement accounts or other benefits for City employees and make
contributions thereto on behalf of such employees. (Ord., 1-4-1982)B. Social
Security:1. It is hereby declared to be the policy and purpose of the City to
extend to the eligible employees thereof 1 , effective as of January 1, 1955,
the benefits of the Federal old age and survivors insurance system, as
authorized by the Federal Social Security Act and amendments thereto.2. The
Mayor is hereby authorized and directed to execute an agreement with the State
employees' retirement system of the State of Illinois (social security unit) to
secure coverage of eligible employees as provided herein.3. Withholdings from
salaries or wages of employees are hereby authorized to be made in the amounts
and at such times as may be required by applicable State or Federal laws or
regulations, and shall be paid over to the State agency in such amounts and at
such times as are designated by State laws or regulations, and employer
contributions and administrative expenses shall be paid to the State agency in
accordance with applicable State laws and regulations from amounts appropriated
for such purposes. (Ord., 11-4-1955)
