whose rights in and to such real estate have arisen subsequent to the weed
cutting and prior to the filing of such notice, and the lien shall not be valid
as to any mortgagee, judgment creditor or other lienor whose rights in and to
such real estate arise prior to the filing of such notice as evidenced by a
properly recorded instrument evidencing such interest, unless said mortgagee,
judgment creditor or other lienor had notice of the unlawful condition as
prohibited in this chapter at any time prior to the remediation of said
unlawful condition. Upon payment of all costs of recording and charges incurred
by the city for the remediation, the city shall release any lien recorded
pursuant to this chapter. (Ord. 13-08, 10-14-2013)
9-5-6: DISCHARGE AND MAINTENANCE OF YARD WASTE:
No yard waste shall be kept in such a manner as to violate any provision of
this code and shall not be placed so as to obstruct pedestrian or vehicular
traffic and shall not obstruct any storm drain. No yard waste may be discharged
onto any public street, sidewalk, or other public right of way, unless such
waste so discharged occurs as the result of the immediate care and maintenance
of property immediately adjacent to the location of such yard waste so
discharged and such yard waste is removed within two (2) hours of being
discharged or prior to any interruption in the maintenance operation so
undertaken, whichever is sooner. Any violation of this section shall be
punishable as provided for in section
1-4-1 of this code, and each day such violation continues to exist shall
constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 13-08, 10-14-2013)
9-5-7: PUBLIC RIGHTS OF WAY:
It shall be the policy of the city that owners, lessees or occupants of real
property which abuts a public right of way, including ditches, boulevards, or
other similar areas, shall be responsible for mowing said right of way areas
which lie immediately adjacent to the property owned, leased or occupied by
such persons and keeping such areas free from the accumulation of yard waste,
litter and debris. (Ord. 13-08, 10-14-2013)
TITLE 10
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
10-1-1: Established
10-1-2: Chief Of Police
10-1-3: Police Officers
10-1-4: Temporary Police
10-1-5: Performance Of Duty
10-1-6: Report Violations To Superior Officer
10-1-7: Powers And Duties
10-1-8: Duties Regarding Gaming Houses
10-1-9: Neglect And Violation Of Duty
10-1-10: Compensation; Uniform
10-1-1: ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby established a department of the city which shall be known as
the police department, which shall embrace one chief of police and such other
number of police officers as may from time to time be fixed by the city
council. (1925 Code § 30-1; amd. 1981 Code)
10-1-2: CHIEF OF POLICE:
   A.   Appointment And Term: The chief of police shall be appointed by the
mayor, by and with the approval of the city council, at the regular meeting in
the month of May, or as soon thereafter as may be, and monthly thereafter. He
shall hold his office for the term of one year and until his successor shall be
appointed and qualified. (1925 Code § 30-2; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   Duties: The chief of police shall:
      1.   Management Of Department: Have the management and control of the
police department of the city, subject to the mayor and the rules and
regulations prescribed by the city council. He shall oversee and direct all
police officers under him, assigning to each beats and districts and their
respective hours for service and prescribe such duties as he shall see fit. He
shall, in no case, absent himself from the city without notifying the mayor of
his intended absence when the same is practicable. (1925 Code § 30-3; amd. 1981
Code)
      2.   Preserve Peace: Devote his whole time to the municipal affairs of
the city, to preserve peace, order and safety and the cleanliness thereof, and
to this end, shall execute and enforce all rules and ordinances of the city
council and the orders of the mayor. (1925 Code § 30-4; amd. 1981 Code)
      3.   Attend Fires; Abate Nuisances: Be charged with the duty of
protecting the rights of persons and property and providing proper police
protection at every fire. He shall also take notice of all nuisances and take
proper steps to abate the same. He shall cause to be removed all impediments
and obstructions in the streets, alleys and public places of the city. (1925
Code § 30-5)
      4.   Attend Council Meetings; Issue Processes: Attend all meetings of the
city council and execute all warrants or other legal processes and all orders
required to be executed by him under any ordinance of the city. (1925 Code §
30-6; amd. 2009 Code)
      5.   Report Derelict Members; Suspension: Report to the mayor any member
of the police force who may be guilty of drunkenness, neglect of duty,
disobedience of orders or violation of the standing rules and regulations of
the police department, and during the pendency of any formal charges against
any police officer, the police chief may, with the consent of the mayor,
suspend such officer from duty until such charges may be investigated. (1925
Code § 30-7; amd. 1981 Code)
      6.   Notify City Attorney Of Suits: Notify or cause to be notified the
city attorney of any suits instituted by him or through his department, wherein
the interest of the city may require the presence of the city attorney at the
trial thereof. (1925 Code § 30-8; amd. 1981 Code)
      7.   Keep Records: Keep or cause to be kept books of record of the police
department of all persons arrested or committed by the police officers, showing
the time and place of each arrest, the offense for which the same was made, the
court of record before which said proceeding was tried and the disposition of
such case. (1925 Code § 30-9; amd. 1981 Code)
   C.   Salary: The chief of police shall receive a monthly salary, to be paid
in monthly installments, as decided upon by the city council for a full time
police chief. (1925 Code § 30-10; amd. 1981 Code)
10-1-3: POLICE OFFICERS:
   A.   Appointment And Term: The mayor, by and with the advice and consent of
the chief of police and by and with the consent of the city council, shall
appoint such number of police officers as the city council, by resolution, may
determine to be necessary, who shall hold their offices until their successors
are appointed and qualified, unless sooner discharged as hereinafter provided.
(1925 Code § 30-11; amd. 1981 Code)
   B.   Oath Of Office: Each police officer shall, before he enters upon the
duties of his office, take and subscribe the oath prescribed by law for such
officers. (1925 Code § 30-12; amd. 2009 Code)
   C.   Part Time Police:
      1.   Employment: The city of Virginia may employ part time police
officers from time to time as they deem necessary.
      2.   Duties: A part time police officer shall have all the
responsibilities of a full time police officer and such specific duties as
delineated in the general orders of the Virginia police department, but the
number of hours a part time officer may work within a calendar year is
restricted. Part time police officers shall not be assigned to supervise or
direct full time police officers. Part time police officers shall be trained in
accordance with the Illinois police training act 1  and the rules and
requirements of the ILETSB.
      3.   Hiring Standards: Any person employed as a part time police officer
must meet the following standards:
         a.   Be of good moral character, of temperate habits, of sound health,
and physically and mentally able to perform assigned duties.
         b.   Be at least twenty one (21) years of age.
         c.   Pass a medical examination.
         d.   Possess a high school diploma or GED certificate.
         e.   Possess a valid state of Illinois driver's license.
         f.   Possess no prior felony convictions.
         g.   Any individual who has served in the U.S. military must have been
honorably discharged.
      4.   Discipline: Part time officers shall be under the disciplinary
jurisdiction of the chief of police. Part time police officers serve at the
discretion of the city authorities, shall not have any property rights in said
employment, and may be removed by the city authorities at any time. Part time
police officers shall comply with all applicable rules and general orders
issued by the police department. (Ord. 12-07, 4-9-2012)
 
Notes
1 1. 50 ILCS 705/1 et seq.
10-1-4: TEMPORARY POLICE:
Whenever the mayor shall deem it necessary to establish temporary night
watchmen or police officers, he may, in writing under the corporate seal,
appoint a suitable number of reputable and discrete citizens of the city as
temporary watchmen or police officers, whose powers, duties and liabilities
shall be the same as other watchmen and police officers, and who shall take and
subscribe the same oath. The mayor shall report all such temporary appointments
to the city council at its next regular meeting, and the city council may
continue or discontinue the same in its discretion, and the person so appointed
shall receive such compensation as may be agreed upon by the mayor or as may be
provided by the city council. (1925 Code § 30-13; amd. 2009 Code)
10-1-5: PERFORMANCE OF DUTY:
   A.   The several members of the police force, when on active duty, shall
devote their entire time to the proper discharge of the duties of their office
according to the rules and ordinances of the city and the rules and regulations
of the police department and shall be subject to call at any time. They shall
be regular and prompt in the discharge of their duties and shall obey all
orders of their superiors, and it shall be their special duty to preserve
order, peace and quiet and to enforce the ordinances of the city. (1925 Code §
30-14)
   B.   The police officers of the city shall be civil and respectful to the
public and, upon all occasions, perform their duties with good temper and
discretion and shall not at any time, while upon duty, make use of violent,
threatening or abusive language, and no member shall communicate to any person
any information which may lead to the escape from arrest or punishment of any
person accused of a crime or the violation of any ordinance of the city. (1925
Code § 30-22)
10-1-6: REPORT VIOLATIONS TO SUPERIOR OFFICER:
Every police officer shall report to his superior officer all persons known to
be gamblers, receivers of stolen property, thieves, burglars or disorderly
persons, and also all unlawful or disorderly houses or places in the city
coming to his knowledge, as well as all violators of the laws of the state or
ordinances of the city reported to him, or of which he may be cognizant, and
when it shall come to the knowledge of any member of the police force that any
ordinance has been violated, such member shall forthwith cause a complaint to
be made before a court of record and the proper witnesses to be subpoenaed and
evidence to be produced for the successful prosecution of the defendant. It
shall be the duty of the chief of police and the police officers to serve
promptly all warrants or other processes issued in any case pending under any
law or ordinance of the city before any proper court thereof. (1925 Code § 30-
15; amd. 1981 Code)
10-1-7: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Arrests: Police officers shall have power to arrest all persons in the
city found in the act of violating any ordinance or aiding or abetting in any
such violation, and shall take all such persons so arrested to the place
designated by such ordinance, and while serving or executing or assisting in
the serving or execution of any warrant or process, they shall be vested with
and have all the power conferred on constables by common law and the laws of
the state. (1925 Code § 30-16)
   B.   Serve Processes: Police officers shall have the power and authority to
execute warrants or other legal processes within the corporate limits of the
city and within such distance therefrom as is authorized by law, in all cases
when any ordinance of the city made pursuant to law shall prescribe a penalty
for the violation of any of its provisions by persons residing, acting or doing
business without the limits of the city. (1925 Code § 30-17; amd. 2009 Code)
   C.   Call On Bystanders: Any police officer of the city may, at any time,
call upon any able bodied person of the age eighteen (18) years or over to aid
him in arresting, retaking or holding in custody any persons guilty of having
committed any unlawful act, or charged therewith, or to aid such officer to
prevent the commission of any unlawful act; and whoever shall refuse to so aid
shall incur a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense. (1925 Code § 30-18; amd. 1981 Code; 2009
Code)
10-1-8: DUTIES REGARDING GAMING HOUSES:
   A.   It shall be the duty of all members of the police force to obtain
information and provide said information to the city regarding each house or
other place within the city where games, devices or tables, roulette wheels,
slot machines or other instruments or things for the purpose of gaming are or
may be set up, kept or maintained; and said police officers shall take all
lawful means to suppress and prevent the playing at the tables, games or
devices aforesaid, and for this purpose, when and as often as any one of them
shall have reasonable cause to suspect that any such table, game or device is
set up, kept or maintained as aforesaid, shall forthwith make complaint thereof
before the proper court and obtain a warrant authorizing him to enter any such
house or place or any room within the same, and said police officer shall
thereupon have authority to demand entrance thereto. If such officer is refused
entry, any person so refusing or neglecting to open the door or entrance to
such house or any room within the same, upon application of any police officer
having such warrant, shall forfeit and pay a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1925 Code § 30-19; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   It is hereby made the duty of all police officers to seize any table,
roulette wheel, slot machine, instrument, device or thing used for the purpose
of gaming, and all such tables, instruments, devices or things shall be
destroyed. Any person obstructing or resisting any member of the police force
in the performance of any act of this subsection shall be subject to a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense. (1925 Code § 30-20; amd. 2009 Code)
10-1-9: NEGLECT AND VIOLATION OF DUTY:
Any member of the police force who shall neglect or refuse to perform any
duties required of him by the ordinances of the city or the rules and
regulations of the department, or who shall, in the discharge of his official
duties, be guilty of fraud, favoritism, extortion, oppression or injustice,
shall, in each case, be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code and shall be subject to suspension and removal from office.
(1925 Code § 30-21; amd. 2009 Code)
10-1-10: COMPENSATION; UNIFORM:
Each police officer, temporary police officer or special police officer shall
receive such reasonable compensation as shall be determined by the city council
at the time of his appointment, and each shall wear such uniform as shall be
prescribed by the city council. (1925 Code § 30-24)
CHAPTER 2
MINORS
SECTION:
10-2-1: Curfew
10-2-2: Trick Or Treating Restricted
10-2-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Age And Hour Restrictions: It shall be unlawful for any boy or girl
under the age of seventeen (17) years to be abroad upon the streets, alleys or
public grounds of the city between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight
and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. unless accompanied by some person of lawful age
having said minor in his charge or unless on some errand by permission or
direction of his parent, guardian or employer. Said minor shall not loiter on
the way or make any undue noise by shouting or yelling, or otherwise disturb
the peace and quiet of the city.
   B.   Arrests; Penalty: Any boy or girl who violates any of the provisions of
subsection A of this section shall be subject to arrest without process. Upon
such arrest, said minor shall be taken and delivered to the parent, guardian or
employer of such minor. On a subsequent arrest, such offender shall be taken by
such officer before any court of record in the city for trial and, upon
conviction, shall be fined in any sum not exceeding fifty dollars ($50.00).
(Ord., 12-6-1927; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-2-2: TRICK OR TREATING RESTRICTED:
Trick or treating shall be allowed only on October 31 of each year and only
between the hours of four o'clock (4:00) P.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) P.M.
(Ord., 10-6-1981; amd. 2009 Code)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
10-3-1: Running At Large
10-3-2: Prohibited Acts
10-3-3: Pet Waste Removal
10-3-1: RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any animal of the species of horse, mule, cow,
sheep, goat, swine, goose or chicken, or any dangerous animal, to run or to be
at large at any time within the corporate limits of the city, and whoever,
being the owner or having the control of such animal or animals, shall suffer
or permit the same to be or to run at large in the city in violation of this
subsection shall be subject to a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00)
nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense, together
with the fees for impounding and the expense of keeping such animal or animals
when impounded. (Ord., 7-2-1990; amd. 2009 Code)
   B.   The permitting of any animal to be upon the streets, unfastened and
unattended, whether hitched to a vehicle or not, or the herding of the same
upon the streets shall be deemed running at large under this chapter. (1925
Code § 14-2)
10-3-2: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Driving Animals Through Streets: It shall be unlawful for any horse,
cattle or other domestic animal to be driven loose through the city without
sufficient attendants to keep said animal from trespassing upon lawns or
adjoining lots; and the owner or any person having in charge any such animals
who shall drive the same along and through the streets or alleys of the city
and shall, on so doing, permit or suffer any such animals to go upon such lawns
or lots, shall, for each and every offense, upon conviction, be fined not less
than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00). (1925 Code § 14-3; amd. Ord., 11-6-1982; 2009 Code)
   B.   Cruelty To Animals:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any draft animal of
the species of horse or mule to remain hitched or tied on any of the public
streets or alleys or on any private property for an unreasonable length of time
without providing such animal with proper food and water. (1925 Code § 14-18;
amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
      2.   Whoever shall be guilty of cruelty to animals in any of the ways
hereinafter mentioned shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense: (1925 Code § 28-36; amd. 1981 Code; 2009
Code)
         a.   By overloading, overdriving, overworking, cruelly beating,
torturing, tormenting, mutilating, or cruelly killing any animal or causing or
knowingly allowing the same to be done;
         b.   By unnecessarily failing to provide any animal in his charge or
custody, as owner or otherwise, with proper food, drink and shelter; (1925 Code
§ 28-36; amd. 1981 Code)
         c.   By abandoning any animal; or (1925 Code § 28-36; amd. 1981 Code;
2009 Code)
         d.   By carrying or driving, or causing to be carried or driven or
kept, any animal in an unnecessarily cruel manner. (1925 Code § 28-36; amd.
1981 Code)
   C.   Noisy Animals: No person shall keep or harbor any dog, whelp, bitch,
cow, calf, horse, ass, or other animal shut up or tied up in any yard, house or
other place in the city which, by barking, howling, braying, bawling or other
noises, shall disturb the peace and quiet of any family, citizen or
neighborhood. Every person violating the provisions of this subsection shall,
upon conviction, forfeit and pay a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for every offense. (Ord., 10-2-1989; amd. 2009 Code)
   D.   Animal Fights: Any person who shall, within the city, keep or use or be
in any way connected with the management of any place kept or used for the
fighting or baiting of any dog, cock or other animal, or who shall permit such
place to be kept or used on premises owned, rented or controlled by him, or who
shall frequent or be found therein for the purpose of witnessing such fighting
or baiting shall, in each case, upon conviction, be fined not less than twenty
five dollars ($25.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00).
(1925 Code § 28-10; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-3-3: PET WASTE REMOVAL:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any owner, keeper, or other adult person who
maintains possession or control of a domestic animal to allow said animal to
deposit feces on any public property or any privately owned property unless
owned by said owner, keeper or other adult person.
   B.   Any person who violates this section and does not immediately and
completely remove the feces deposited shall be fined in accordance with the
general penalty provisions set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code or any future amendment thereto. (Ord. 2015-15-07, 7-13-
2015)
ARTICLE A. DOGS AND CATS
SECTION:
10-3A-1: Running At Large Prohibited
10-3A-2: Dogs To Be Leashed
10-3A-3: Muzzles Required
10-3A-4: Females During Estrus
10-3A-5: Dangerous Dogs
10-3A-6: Abandoning Dogs And Cats Prohibited
10-3A-7: Penalty
10-3A-1: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
   A.   Dogs: Any dog found running or being at large in any of the streets,
public ways or upon the private premises of any person, other than the premises
of the owner or keeper thereof, is a public nuisance. No person shall cause or
permit any dog owned or kept by him to be so at large within the city. (Ord.,
5-11-1970)
   B.   Cats: The owner or keeper of any cat shall not permit, cause or suffer
such cat to run at large. The keeping, housing, maintaining, feeding or caring
for any cat shall be deemed prima facie evidence of ownership of such cat.
(Ord., 5-11-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
10-3A-2: DOGS TO BE LEASHED:
All dogs, while on any street, public way or private premises, other than the
premises of the owner, agent or keeper thereof, shall be led by a chain or
leash not exceeding six feet (6') in length in such a manner as to prevent such
dog from biting or otherwise injuring any person or animal. Nothing in this
section shall be interpreted to require the leashing of any dog while on the
private premises of the owner, agent of the owner or keeper thereof, except as
provided in section
10-3A-5 of this article. (Ord., 5-11-1970)
10-3A-3: MUZZLES REQUIRED:
   A.   Proclamation To Muzzle: The mayor shall, when directed so to do by the
county board of health, issue a proclamation prohibiting for a certain time all
dogs on any of the streets, alleys or other public places in the city unless
such dogs be securely muzzled with a wire muzzle so as to effectually prevent
such dogs from biting any person or animal. Said proclamation shall be
published weekly in one or more newspapers of general circulation in the city
during the space of time mentioned in the proclamation. (1925 Code § 14-20;
amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   Unauthorized Removal Of Muzzle: No person shall, without the consent of
the owner or keeper, remove from any dog any muzzle or loosen the same so that
it shall come off. (1925 Code § 14-24; amd. 2009 Code)
10-3A-4: FEMALES DURING ESTRUS:
No owner or keeper of any female dog shall knowingly permit or allow the same
to be upon the public ways of the city while in heat, whether registered or
licensed or not. (1925 Code § 14-23; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-3A-5: DANGEROUS DOGS:
   A.   Definition: As used in this section, the term "dangerous dog" is as
defined in the Illinois animal control act as it now exists or is hereafter
amended 1 . (Ord. 08-07, 9-11-2008)
   B.   Safety Requirements: If a confined dog is so declared to be dangerous,
the owner or keeper of such dog shall immediately provide extraordinary
precautions, such as a muzzle, chain, cage and warning signs, as may be
required by the police department. (Ord., 5-11-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
   C.   Impoundment Costs; Conditions Of Redemption:
      1.   The cost to reclaim a dog that has been deemed a "dangerous dog", as
defined in subsection A of this section, shall be six hundred dollars
($600.00). Additionally, the owner shall be required to deposit the sum of two
hundred dollars ($200.00) with the city, and upon providing evidence to the
police chief that the dog has been spayed or neutered and microchipped within
fourteen (14) days of reclaiming the dog, said deposit shall be refunded to the
owner. If the owner fails to provide said evidence to the police chief within
said time period, the deposit shall be forfeited. Furthermore, a boarding fee
of twenty dollars ($20.00) per day will be assessed, together with a two
hundred dollar ($200.00) pick up fee.
      2.   In the event the dog is impounded for a second incident, the owner
of the dog, or other responsible person, shall be fined one thousand dollars
($1,000.00). A one thousand five hundred dollar ($1,500.00) fine shall be
imposed for a third incident. Upon a fourth incident, the dog will be humanely
euthanized.
      3.   Nothing in this subsection is intended to abrogate any of the powers
granted to the police department in the treatment of dogs within the city.
(Ord. 08-07, 9-11-2008)
 
Notes
1 1. 510 ILCS 5/1 et seq.
10-3A-6: ABANDONING DOGS AND CATS PROHIBITED:
No person may bring into the city any dog or cat and thereafter leave, abandon
and place said dog or cat within the city on any public property or private
property not owned or in the legal possession of the person so bringing the dog
or cat into the city. (Ord., 5-11-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
10-3A-7: PENALTY:
   A.   Any person violating any provision of this article shall, upon
conviction, be fined no less than two hundred dollars ($200.00) and no more
than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) per occurrence.
   B.   If while running at large the animal attacks, bites, injures or
attempts to attack, bite or injure any person or another animal, such action
shall be considered a separate offense and a fine of no less than five hundred
dollars ($500.00) and no more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) shall
be imposed. The penalty provided under this section shall be in addition to any
other remedy available to the city under this code and/or as provided by state
law. (Ord. 13-05, 5-13-2013)
ARTICLE B. KEEPING OF DOMESTIC FOWL
SECTION:
10-3B-1: Definitions
10-3B-2: Limit To Number Of Hens Permitted
10-3B-3: Confinement
10-3B-4: Structures - Location Restrictions
10-3B-5: Structures - Requirements
10-3B-6: Maintenance Of Sanitary Conditions
10-3B-7: Miscellaneous Regulations
10-3B-8: License And Permit Required
10-3B-9: License Permit Process
10-3B-10: Suspension Or Revocation
10-3B-11: Removal Of Structures
10-3B-12: Conflict With Private Covenants
10-3B-13: Penalty For Violation
10-3B-1: DEFINITIONS:
Whenever the following words or phrases are used, they shall, for the purposes
of this article, have the meaning ascribed to them in this section, except when
the context otherwise indicates:
COOP: A structure housing hens consisting of a covered inside enclosure.
HEN: As used in this article, the female of the species Gallus Domesticus
(chicken), Anser Domesticus or Anser Cygnoides (geese), Meleagris Gallopavo
(domesticated turkey), Anas platyrhynchos (duck) commonly known as domestic
fowl.
PEN: An enclosure connected to a coop for the purposes of allowing domestic
fowl to leave the coop while remaining in an enclosed, predator safe
environment. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-2: LIMIT TO NUMBER OF HENS PERMITTED:
No person shall keep more than eight (8) hens. Male species shall be
prohibited. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-3: CONFINEMENT:
All hens kept in the City shall be entirely confined in a pen, coop, building,
or other enclosure at all times. During daylight hours hens may also be
temporarily kept in a mobile screened enclosure commonly known as a domestic
fowl tractor. Such domestic fowl tractors shall be located only in a rear yard
in accordance with the structures - location restrictions provided for in this
article. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-4: STRUCTURES - LOCATION RESTRICTIONS:
Structures housing hens including any pens, coops, buildings or enclosures
shall be permitted only in conjunction with a single- family detached dwelling
located in a residential district. Structures housing hens including any pens,
coops, buildings or enclosures shall be located only in a rear yard, erected or
maintained at least twenty feet (20') from any occupied residential structure
other than that of the owner, set back at least six feet (6') from all property
lines of an adjacent property and shall not be visible from a street. (Ord.
2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-5: STRUCTURES - REQUIREMENTS:
Structures housing hens shall consist of a covered inside enclosure known as a
coop and an adjacent covered outside fenced area known as a pen. Structures
housing hens shall provide not less than five (5) square feet per hen with coop
size limited to not more than fifty (50) square feet and pen enclosures limited
to not more than one hundred (100) square feet. Coops shall be constructed
above ground or on a hard surface such as concrete, patio block or gravel and
able to withstand natural forces such as wind, rain and snow. Wooden or pre-
cast concrete posts shall be acceptable foundations if they are placed at least
twenty four inches (24") into the ground and firmly tamped with dirt or gravel.
Any structure housing hens including any pen, coop, building or other enclosure
that is not fully enclosed shall be screened to a height of six feet (6'). Said
screening shall be comprised of fences or walls six feet (6') in height. (Ord.
2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-6: MAINTENANCE OF SANITARY CONDITIONS:
All pens, coops, buildings, yards or enclosures for hens shall be kept clean,
sanitary and free from all refuse and waste. Such areas shall be thoroughly
cleaned at least once every twenty four (24) hours and all refuse and domestic
fowl waste shall be disposed of in a clean and sanitary fashion. (Ord. 2016-16-
1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-7: MISCELLANEOUS REGULATIONS:
   A.   All feed for hens shall be kept in rodent proof containers until put
out for consumption by the permitted hens being kept.
   B.   Slaughtering of domestic fowl for sale or gift is prohibited.
   C.   Odors from domestic fowl, domestic fowl manure or other domestic fowl
related substances shall not be perceptible at the property boundaries of the
property where the domestic fowl are kept, and it is hereby declared a nuisance
and shall be unlawful for any person to allow such nuisance to exist.
   D.   No person shall allow domestic fowl to provide noise loud enough to
annoy or disturb the comfort, health, peace or repose of reasonable persons of
ordinary sensibilities, and it is hereby declared a nuisance and shall be
unlawful for any person to allow such nuisance to exist. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-
2016)
10-3B-8: LICENSE AND PERMIT REQUIRED:
No person shall keep domestic fowl within the City without first obtaining a
license therefor issued by the City. Any pen, coop, building or other enclosure
used for the housing of hens may be erected only after obtaining a building
permit as provided for herein. Only landowners shall be eligible to make
application for license. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-9: LICENSE PERMIT PROCESS:
   A.   An applicant for a license for the keeping of domestic fowl or for a
building permit for any pen, coop, building or other enclosure used for the
housing of domestic fowl must submit the following to the Public Works
Director:
      1.   Completed applications on forms provided by the City.
      2.   A current plat of survey or other drawing accurately depicting the
potential location of the proposed structure housing hens on the applicant's
property.
      3.   The required building permit fee. The building permit fee for a pen,
coop, building or other enclosure used for the housing of domestic fowl shall
be the same fee as for a shed.
   B.   A license for the keeping of domestic fowl and a building permit for a
structure for the keeping of domestic fowl shall not be granted unless the
applicant can show proof that a proposed structure that complies with all
provisions of this article will be erected.
   C.   A license for keeping of domestic fowl and a building permit for a
structure for the keeping of domestic fowl shall not be transferable or run
with the land and shall terminate and become invalid upon the licensee no
longer occupying the property for which the license and permit were issued.
(Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-10: SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION:
In addition to any other penalty which may be authorized by this article or
other City ordinances, the Mayor may suspend or revoke any license issued
pursuant to this article for:
   A.   Failure of the licensee to comply with any provisions of this article,
any other applicable ordinances, the laws of the State, Federal laws or other
applicable legal requirements; or
   B.   Finding that the licensee knowingly furnished false or misleading
information or withheld relevant information in any application for a license
for the keeping of domestic fowl or for a building permit for any structure for
the keeping of domestic fowl. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-11: REMOVAL OF STRUCTURES:
Structures housing hens including any pens, coops, buildings or enclosures
shall be removed upon a licensee no longer keeping domestic fowl, upon a
licensee no longer occupying the property for which a license for the keeping
of domestic fowl was issued or upon a licensee for the keeping of domestic fowl
having been revoked. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-12: CONFLICT WITH PRIVATE COVENANTS:
Nothing in this article shall be construed to permit the keeping of domestic
fowl when such activity is prohibited by private covenants, conditions or
restrictions governing the use of property. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
10-3B-13: PENALTY FOR VIOLATION:
   A.   Any person violating any of the provisions or failure to comply with
any of the mandatory requirements of this article shall be guilty of an offense
and shall be fined in accordance with the general penalty provided by this
Code.
   B.   Any person shall be guilty of a separate offense for each and every day
during any portion of which any violation or provision of this article is
committed, continued or permitted by any such person, and such person shall be
punished accordingly. (Ord. 2016-16-1, 2-8-2016)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL OFFENSES
ARTICLE A. OFFENSES RELATING TO PEACE AND SAFETY
SECTION:
10-4A-1: Assault; Affrays
10-4A-2: Disturbing The Peace
10-4A-3: Unlawful Assemblies
10-4A-4: Resisting Officers; Aiding Escape
10-4A-5: Weapons
10-4A-6: False Fire Alarms
10-4A-7: Penalty
10-4A-1: ASSAULT; AFFRAYS:
No person shall assault, strike or beat another or, by mutual agreement, fight
another, nor shall such person be guilty of an affray or any conduct calculated
to provoke a breach of the peace. (1925 Code § 28-1; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4A-2: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
No person shall disturb the public peace and quiet of the city or of any
private family or citizen, or shall be guilty of any violent, tumultuous,
offensive or disorderly conduct, or breach of the peace, or shall make any loud
or unusual noises or disturbance, or shall use any obscene, profane, vulgar or
unseemly language, or shall conduct himself in a riotous manner, or shall aid,
countenance or assist in the said violations. (1925 Code § 28-2; amd. 1981
Code; 2009 Code)
10-4A-3: UNLAWFUL ASSEMBLIES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any two (2) or more persons to assemble
together within the city for any unlawful purpose or, when being assembled, to
act in concert to do an unlawful act with force and violence against the
property of the city or the person or property of another, or against the
peace, or to the terror of citizens or other persons, or to make any movement
or preparation therefor. It shall further be unlawful for said persons to
refuse to disperse after being requested so to do by any police officer or
other conservator of the peace. (1925 Code § 28-5; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   No person shall knowingly suffer or permit any assemblage for the
purpose of committing any unlawful act or breach of the peace or any riotous,
offensive or disorderly conduct in or upon premises owned or occupied by him or
under his control within the city. (1925 Code § 28-6; amd. 1981 Code; 2009
Code)
10-4A-4: RESISTING OFFICERS; AIDING ESCAPE:
No person shall wilfully hinder, delay, resist or obstruct any officer of the
city or any person aiding him in the discharge of any official duty, and no
person shall rescue or attempt to rescue any person from the custody of any
officer or any person having such person legally in custody, or shall molest or
interfere with any officer or person so having any person in custody. (1925
Code § 28-7; amd. 2009 Code)
10-4A-5: WEAPONS:
   A.   Concealed Weapons: It shall be unlawful for any person, within the
limits of the city and without a permit obtained therefor as provided by law,
to carry or wear under his clothes or concealed about his person any pistol,
revolver, derringer, bowie knife, dirk, razor, dagger, slingshot, metallic
knuckles or other weapons; provided, however, the provisions of this subsection
shall not apply to sheriffs, coroners, constables, the chief of police, police
officers or other peace officers in the discharge of their official duties.
(1925 Code § 28-8; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   Discharging Firearms: No person shall fire or discharge any gun, pistol
or other firearm within the corporate limits of the city. (1925 Code § 20-7;
amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4A-6: FALSE FIRE ALARMS:
No person, without a reasonable cause, by outcry or otherwise, shall make or
circulate, or cause to be made or circulated, any false alarm of fire. (1925
Code § 19-19; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4A-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this article, upon conviction, shall be
fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense. (2009 Code)
ARTICLE B. OFFENSES RELATING TO MORALS AND DECENCY
SECTION:
10-4B-1: Intoxication Or Drunkenness Prohibited
10-4B-2: Indecent Exposure
10-4B-3: Gambling
10-4B-4: Penalty For Intoxication/Drunkenness, Indecent Exposure And Gambling
10-4B-5: Possession Of Cannabis Or The Synthetic Form Commonly Known As K2
Prohibited
10-4B-6: Possession Of Drug Paraphernalia
10-4B-7: Penalties For Possession Of Cannabis, K2 Or Drug Paraphernalia;
Application Of Fines
10-4B-1: INTOXICATION OR DRUNKENNESS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to be in a state of intoxication or
drunkenness and acting in such a manner as to disturb or breach the peace, or
act disorderly, or endanger him/herself or another, within the corporate limits
of the City, regardless of whether such intoxication or drunkenness occurs in
any public or private place.
Being intoxicated or in a state of drunkenness shall not be the sole basis for
the offense of drunkenness or intoxication 1 .
A person who appears to be intoxicated or drunk in a public place and who may
be in or a danger to himself or others may be assisted to his home, a treatment
facility, or other health/hospital facility either directly by the police or
through an intermediary person. Such person shall be detained for protective
custody purposes only, and shall not be cited and/or arrested 2 . (Ord. 2018-
18-6, 7-9-2018)
 
Notes
1 1. 20 ILCS 301/55-15.
2 2. 20 ILCS 301/25-15.
10-4B-2: INDECENT EXPOSURE:
No person shall, purposely, publicly make any indecent exposure of his or her
person, or shall appear on the streets in a public place in a state of nudity,
or shall be guilty of any other like indecent or lewd act or misbehavior. (1925
Code § 28-12; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4B-3: GAMBLING 1 , 2 :
   A.   Prohibited Generally: No person shall deal, play or engage in faro,
roulette or any other device or game of chance, either as banker, dealer,
player or otherwise, for the purpose of gaming. (1925 Code § 28-16; amd. 1981
Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   Gaming On Streets: No person shall expose, in any of the streets,
avenues or other public places within the limits of the City, any table or
device of any kind whatever, upon or by which any game of chance or hazard can
be played, or shall play at or upon any such table or device. (1925 Code § 28-
17; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   C.   Keeping Gambling House And Gambling Devices: No person shall, within
the City, set up, keep, maintain or support any gambling house or room or place
used for the practice of gaming or playing for money or property, or shall
knowingly permit any building or premises owned or controlled by him to be used
for any such purpose, or shall keep or use, or permit to be kept or used, in
any building or place occupied, controlled or owned by such person any keno or
faro table, poker table, crap layout, wheel of fortune, roulette,
shuffleboards, slot machine, cards or other instruments or devices commonly
used for the purpose of gaming, or shall keep or have in his possession any
such gaming instruments or devices for the purpose of gaming therewith. (1925
Code § 28-15; amd. 2009 Code)
   D.   Frequenting Gambling Houses: No person shall patronize, visit, frequent
or be connected with the management of, or shall serve as doorkeeper, runner,
solicitor or agent of any house, room or other premises kept within the City
for the purpose of permitting others to gamble for any thing, or shall be found
therein, and no person shall, in any manner, play, raffle, bet or otherwise
gamble for any thing or shall bet on any game, lot, chance or hazard upon which
others may be playing. (1925 Code § 28-18; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   E.   Exceptions To Subsections A Through D Of This Section: Video gaming
shall be allowed within the City limits in licensed establishments in
accordance with the Illinois Video Gaming Act, as heretofore established or
hereafter amended. (Ord. 12-15, 8-13-2012)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  10-1-8 of this title for Police Department duties.
2 2. See also title 8, chapter 6 of this Code.
10-4B-4: PENALTY FOR INTOXICATION/DRUNKENNESS, INDECENT EXPOSURE AND GAMBLING:
Any person violating any provision of sections
10-4B-1,
10-4B-2, and
10-4B-3 of this article, upon conviction, shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each offense. (Ord. 2018-18-6, 7-9-2018)
10-4B-5: POSSESSION OF CANNABIS OR THE SYNTHETIC FORM COMMONLY KNOWN AS K2
PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person shall possess 10.0 grams or less of any substance containing
cannabis, or the synthetic form of cannabis, 1-pentyl-3(1-napthoyl)indole,
commonly known as K2.
   B.   For the purpose of this section, cannabis includes marijuana, hashish,
and other substances which are identified as including any parts of the plant
cannabis sativa, whether growing or not; the seeds thereof, the resin extracted
from any part of such plant; and any compound, manufacture, salt, derivative,
and all other cannabinol derivatives, including its naturally occurring or
synthetically produced ingredients, whether produced directly or indirectly by
extraction, or independently by means of chemical synthesis or by a combination
of extraction and chemical synthesis; but shall not include the mature stalks
of such plant, fiber produced from such stalks, oil or cake made from the seeds
of such plant, any other compound, manufacture, salt, derivative, mixture or
preparation of such mature stalks (except the resin extracted therefrom),
fiber, oil or cake, or the sterilized seed of such plant which is incapable of
germination. (Ord. 2018-18-6, 7-9-2018)
10-4B-6: POSSESSION OF DRUG PARAPHERNALIA:
   A.   No person shall knowingly possess any item of drug paraphernalia with
the intent to use it for the purpose of unlawfully ingesting, inhaling or
otherwise introducing cannabis or a controlled substance into the human body.
   B.   As used in this section, the following terms shall include and have the
following meanings:
    CANNABIS: Shall mean and include any substance defined as cannabis in
section 3 of the Illinois Cannabis Control Act, 720 Illinois Compiled Statutes
550/3.
   DRUG PARAPHERNALIA: Means any object or device used, designed for use or
intended for use in unlawfully ingesting, smoking, administering, or storing
cannabis. For the purposes of this section, drug paraphernalia includes but is
not limited to:
   A.   Metal, wooden, plastic, glass, stone or ceramic pipes, with or without
screens;
   B.   Water pipes;
   C.   Carburetion tubes and devices;
   D.   Smoking and carburetion masks;
   E.   Roach clips;
   F.   Bongs; and
   G.   One-hitters. (Ord. 2018-18-6, 7-9-2018)
10-4B-7: PENALTIES FOR POSSESSION OF CANNABIS, K2 OR DRUG PARAPHERNALIA;
APPLICATION OF FINES:
   A.   Any person violating any provision of section
10-4B-5 or
10-4B-6 of this article, upon conviction, shall be fined no less than one
hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00) per violation. Possession of each gram of cannabis or K2 or each item
of drug paraphernalia may be considered a separate offense. In addition to any
fine imposed for violation of section
10-4B-5 or
10-4B-6 of this article, the violator shall be responsible for reimbursement of
the City's reasonable attorneys' fees and costs incurred in connection with the
prosecution of the ordinance violation as set forth in section
1-4-4 of this Code.
   B.   For every violation of section
10-4B-5 or
10-4B-6 of this article, after reimbursing the City's General Fund for the
attorneys' fees and costs incurred in connection with the prosecution of the
ordinance violation, any fines collected shall be deposited in the City's
General Police Fund for use as determined by the Chief of Police or City
Council. (Ord. 2018-18-6, 7-9-2018)
ARTICLE C. OFFENSES INVOLVING PROPERTY
SECTION:
10-4C-1: Damage To Property
10-4C-2: Auctions In Public Ways
10-4C-3: Throwing Glass On Streets
10-4C-4: Removing Cornerstones
10-4C-5: Penalty
10-4C-1: DAMAGE TO PROPERTY:
   A.   No person shall wilfully, maliciously or negligently break, deface,
destroy or otherwise injure any public property of the state, county or city or
any private property. (1925 Code § 28-29; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
   B.   No person shall wilfully, maliciously or negligently, in any manner,
injure, deface, remove or destroy any fruit, ornamental or shade tree, or
boxing placed around the same, or any shrub, fence, railing, gate or sign upon
any public grounds, sidewalk or private premises, or any bridge, sewer,
culvert, drain or sidewalk, or shall trespass upon any private premises or
public grounds and injure, carry away or destroy any tree, fruit, vegetable,
plant, shrub or other thing which may be therein for ornament or otherwise, or
shall obstruct any public or private doorway or entrance with boxes or other
things to the hindrance or danger of the occupant of the premises, or remove
any gate from its hinges or other fixtures, for mischief. (1925 Code § 28-30;
amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4C-2: AUCTIONS IN PUBLIC WAYS:
No person shall be permitted to occupy any of the public streets, sidewalks or
alleyways in the city for the purpose of conducting an auction sale or for the
purpose of vending at auction or otherwise any goods, wares, merchandise or
patent medicines, and no person shall violate any of the provisions of this
section after being notified by the chief of police or any police officer of
the city to desist therefrom. (1925 Code § 27-14; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4C-3: THROWING GLASS ON STREETS:
No person shall throw, cast or lay or place upon any streets within the city
any glass, bottles, window glass or other articles made of or containing glass,
and in case of any accident causing the breaking of any glass upon any such
street, the owner or person in charge of such glass, or the persons responsible
for such breakage, shall at once remove or cause the same to be removed from
the street. (1925 Code § 35-21)
10-4C-4: REMOVING CORNERSTONES:
No person shall wilfully or heedlessly remove or destroy any stone, stake or
post set or placed to mark the corner of any lot, any parcel of ground, or any
street or alley, or to show the grade of any street or alley of the city. (1925
Code § 28-35; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
10-4C-5: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this article, upon conviction, shall be
fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense. (2009 Code)
TITLE 11
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS
SECTION:
11-1-1: Definitions
11-1-2: Police Department To Enforce
11-1-3: Licenses And Permits Required
11-1-4: Through Streets And Stop Intersections
11-1-5: Speed Limits
11-1-6: Obstructing Intersections
11-1-7: Traffic Flow During Annual Barbecue
11-1-8: Driving Through Processions
11-1-9: Toy Vehicles On Sidewalks
11-1-10: Driving While Intoxicated; Restitution For Emergency Response
11-1-11: Repairing Vehicles On Streets
11-1-12: Leaving Vehicle Unattended
11-1-13: Penalty
11-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
BOULEVARD: Applies to that portion of the City right-of-way or other premises
between a curb and the sidewalk.
CURB: Applies to the boundaries of a "street", as defined in this section.
DRIVER: Applies to the rider, driver or leader of a horse and a person who
pushes, draws, propels or operates or who is in charge of a vehicle.
HORSE: Applies to any draft animal or beast of burden.
PARK, PARKED AND PARKING: Refers to any vehicle waiting or standing in any
street or alley except when such vehicle is waiting in compliance with the
direction of a traffic officer or to meet others driving emergency vehicles.
STREET: Applies to that part of the public highway intended for vehicles.
STREET INTERSECTION: Applies to any street which joins another at an angle,
whether or not it crosses the other street.
VEHICLE: Applies to a horse, motor vehicle, motorcycle, trailer, and to any
conveyance. (1925 Code § 35-26; amd. 2009 Code; Ord. 22-4, 9-12-2022)
11-1-2: POLICE DEPARTMENT TO ENFORCE:
The police department is hereby authorized, empowered and ordered to exercise
all powers and duties in relation to the management of street traffic and to
direct, control, stop, restrict and regulate, and when necessary, temporarily
divert or exclude, in the interest of public safety, health and convenience,
the movement of pedestrians and animal and vehicular traffic of every kind in
the streets and parks and on bridges in the city. (1925 Code § 35-24)
11-1-3: LICENSES AND PERMITS REQUIRED:
   A.   No person shall drive any motor vehicle upon a street or alleyway
unless such person has a valid license or permit or restricted driving permit
issued by the secretary of state of the state of Illinois, or by some other
state.
   B.   No motor vehicle shall be operated on any street or alleyway without
first complying with all requirements for registration and certification with
the secretary of state of the state of Illinois or with some other state.
(Ord., 7-2-1979; amd. 2009 Code)
11-1-4: THROUGH STREETS AND STOP INTERSECTIONS:
   A.   Through Streets Authorized; Vehicle Operation: The city council may, by
resolution passed at a regular meeting of the council, designate certain
streets within the city as through streets for the purpose of regulating the
traffic on said streets. Any person driving a vehicle on or along any street
designated as a through street shall have the right of way over all persons
driving upon and along any intersecting streets, and the city council may, in
said resolution, provide that there be placed upon the pavement of intersecting
streets or other conspicuous places, signs requiring all vehicles to come to a
stop before crossing such through streets.
   B.   Stops At Through Street Intersections: The following stop signs are
hereby erected to regulate the flow of traffic on through streets in the city:
