   C.   Three-Way Stop Intersections: The following intersections are three-way
stop intersections in the city, and all traffic approaching said intersections,
vehicular or otherwise, shall stop before entering:
South East Street and Broadway Street
Sylvan Street and North Cass Street
(1925 Code § 35-23; amd. Ord., 3-5-1990; Ord. 06-08, 8-14-2006; Ord. 2019-07,
9-12-2019)
11-1-5: SPEED LIMITS:
Every driver operating a vehicle on a street within the city shall drive the
same in a careful and prudent manner and at all times have the vehicle under
control and at a rate of speed not more than twenty five (25) miles per hour
unless otherwise posted. (1925 Code § 35-1; amd. 2009 Code)
11-1-6: OBSTRUCTING INTERSECTIONS:
No person shall stop any automobile, truck or other vehicle for pleasure or
burden on any of the crossings in the streets of the city so as to
inconvenience persons crossing the same or shall in any other manner obstruct
any crossing, except so far as may be necessary in crossing the same. (1925
Code § 28-25; amd. 1981 Code; 2009 Code)
11-1-7: TRAFFIC FLOW DURING ANNUAL BARBECUE:
During the 2006 Virginia City BBQ and all Virginia City BBQs held thereafter,
traffic patterns will be modified as follows and as shown on the diagram
attached to ordinance 06-01 as exhibit A, and made a part hereof:
Front Street, one-way southbound from Jackson Street to Springfield Street to
allow for angle parking.
Jackson Street, one-way westbound from Main Street to Front Street.
Springfield Street, one-way westbound from Front Street to North Second West
Street. (Ord. 06-01, 3-13-2006)
11-1-8: DRIVING THROUGH PROCESSIONS:
It shall be unlawful for a driver of any vehicle to drive or lead his vehicle
through any funeral procession or any parade authorized by the mayor within the
limits of the city. (1925 Code § 35-15)
11-1-9: TOY VEHICLES ON SIDEWALKS 1 :
The use of bicycles, skateboards, scooters, roller blades and similar wheeled
devices on the sidewalks of the Virginia city square is hereby prohibited. This
section specifically does not apply to wheelchairs and scooters used by
disabled persons to provide mobility. (Ord., 8-5-2002)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  3-1-10 of this code.
11-1-10: DRIVING WHILE INTOXICATED; RESTITUTION FOR EMERGENCY RESPONSE:
   A.   Prohibition: It shall be unlawful for any person, while in an
intoxicated condition, to drive any vehicle upon the streets of the city. (1925
Code § 35-16)
   B.   Emergency Response Restitution:
      1.   Definition: As used in this subsection, "emergency response" means
any incident requiring a response by a police officer, a firefighter carried on
the rolls of a regularly constituted fire department, or an ambulance.
      2.   Fee Established: Any individual convicted of or who pleads guilty to
and is placed on supervision for a violation of 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes
5/11-501, section 5-7 of the snowmobile registration and safety act 1 , section
5-16 of the boat registration and safety act 2 , or a similar provision, whose
operation of a motor vehicle, snowmobile, or watercraft while in violation of
625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-501, section 5-7 of the snowmobile
registration and safety act, section 5-16 of the boat registration and safety
act, or a similar provision, proximately caused an incident resulting in an
appropriate emergency response shall be required to make restitution to the
city for the costs of that emergency response. The restitution may not exceed
one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) per agency for each emergency response.
      3.   Information To State: The city police chief and city fire chief are
hereby authorized and directed to promptly advise the appropriate state's
attorney of the city's desire to seek said restitution in such instances as
defined under subsection B2 of this section, and to provide the state's
attorney with such further information necessary as to the costs associated
with said emergency response.
      4.   Action To Recover Costs: In the event the appropriate state's
attorney declines to seek the requested restitution, the city attorney is
hereby authorized to maintain a separate action to recover the costs associated
with said emergency response, and in such instance, said person(s) shall be
liable to the city for reasonable attorney fees and costs incurred to recover
said costs associated with said emergency response. (Ord. 08-05, 7-14-2008)
 
Notes
1 1. 625 ILCS 40/5-7.
2 2. 625 ILCS 45/5-16.
11-1-11: REPAIRING VEHICLES ON STREETS:
No person shall adjust or repair any automobile or motorcycle or race the motor
of same while standing on the public streets or alleys of the city, except in
the case of a breakdown or other emergency requiring same, and no person or
employee connected with a garage or repair shop shall use the streets or alleys
in the vicinity of such garage or shop for the purpose of working on or upon
automobiles or motor driven vehicles of any description. (1925 Code § 35-19)
11-1-12: LEAVING VEHICLE UNATTENDED:
It shall be unlawful for the operator of any motor vehicle or person in charge
thereof to leave unattended upon any street or highway a motor vehicle with the
engine running. (1925 Code § 35-20)
11-1-13: PENALTY:
Unless otherwise provided, a violation of any provision of this title shall be
punishable by a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1925 Code § 35-25; amd. 2009 Code)
CHAPTER 2
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
11-2-1: Method Of Parking
11-2-2: Leaving Parking Spaces
11-2-3: No Parking Places; General Parking Restrictions
11-2-4: No Parking On Specific Streets And Places
11-2-5: Limited Parking On Certain Streets And Places
11-2-6: Parking Trucks, Tractors And Commercial Vehicles
11-2-7: Loading And Unloading
11-2-8: Parking For Persons With Disabilities
11-2-9: Payment Of Fines; Responsibility For Additional Costs
11-2-10: Winter Parking Restrictions
11-2-11: Compact Vehicle Parking
11-2-1: METHOD OF PARKING:
   A.   Parallel Parking: Vehicles shall be parked parallel to the curb as
provided herein and shall be placed so that neither right wheel, or the left
wheel when in the far left lane of a one-way street, shall be further than
eighteen inches (18") from the curb and not nearer than four feet (4') to
either end of any other standing vehicle. This subsection shall not apply to
parking on the public square as provided by resolution of the city council.
(1925 Code § 35-9; amd. 2009 Code)
   B.   Angle Parking In Residence Districts: There shall be no angle parking
on any of the streets in the residence portion of the city, and no parking
space shall be marked off in any part of the residence portion of the city.
(1925 Code § 35-10)
   C.   Parking In Marked Spaces: The city council may, by resolution duly
passed by a majority vote of the council at any regular or special meeting
called for that purpose, designate portions of streets in the city as parking
spaces and mark off said parking space by appropriate markers, either for
parallel or angle parking, and when any such parking space has been designated,
it shall be unlawful for any person to park except upon the space thus marked
off. (1925 Code § 35-11)
11-2-2: LEAVING PARKING SPACES:
The driver of a parked vehicle about to start shall give moving vehicles the
right of way, and the driver of the parked vehicle shall give a timely and
visible warning in some unmistakable manner before starting. (1925 Code § 35-
12)
11-2-3: NO PARKING PLACES; GENERAL PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   No vehicle shall be parked within twenty five feet (25') of any stop
sign or within fifteen feet (15') of the projected property line of any street
or alley intersection.
   B.   No vehicle shall be left standing in such a manner as to obstruct any
crosswalk or private driveway.
   C.   No vehicle shall be parked within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
   D.   No vehicle shall be parked in any street for the purpose of exhibition
or sale. (1925 Code § 35-13; amd. 2009 Code)
   E.   On the streets of the city commonly called "alleys", no vehicle shall
be parked except for the purpose of actually loading or unloading and, in no
case, shall a vehicle be parked so as to obstruct traffic in any alley. (1925
Code § 35-22)
   F.   It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave unattended any
motor vehicle upon any sidewalk within the city. (Ord., 10-4-1982; amd. 2009
Code)
   G.   1. The parking of motor vehicles on any street, alley or highway owned
or maintained by the city shall be regulated as follows:
         a.   No motor vehicle shall be allowed to be parked or otherwise left
standing, with or without the motor running, so as to block the ingress or
egress to any business or residence within the city.
         b.   No person shall be allowed to park or otherwise leave standing
any motor vehicle upon any street, alley or highway owned or maintained by the
city so as to impede the efficient removal of snow from said street, alley or
highway.
      2.   The chief of police of the city may, at his or her discretion,
request the removal of any motor vehicle from any street, alley or highway
within the city if, in the sole opinion and discretion of said chief of police,
said motor vehicle impedes in any way the normal course of traffic upon any
street, alley or highway within the city. In such event, the chief of police
shall give the owner of said motor vehicle written notice to remove said motor
vehicle within twenty four (24) hours, and said owner's failure to remove said
vehicle to a position which does not impede traffic as aforesaid shall be
punishable by the imposition of a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code.
   H.   The parking of campers and/or recreational vehicles on city streets and
rights of way is hereby prohibited.
   I.   No vehicle shall stop, park or stand idle, with or without the motor
running, on the boulevard. This prohibition shall not apply to police, fire,
ambulance or other emergency vehicles during emergencies or drills therefor.
Nor shall the prohibition herein apply to tow trucks removing vehicles in
violation of this section of the City Code of Ordinances. (Ord., 4-6-1987; amd.
Ord., 2001; 2009 Code; Ord. 22-4, 9-12-2022)
11-2-4: NO PARKING ON SPECIFIC STREETS AND PLACES:
Cass County Courthouse:
No vehicle shall be parked in any street, crosswalk, intersection or place,
other than a marked parking space, on any street surrounding or comprising the
Cass County Courthouse.
Cass Street:
There is hereby created a no parking zone for the entire length of the east
side of Cass Street between Springfield and Myrtle Streets within the city. Any
person who causes any vehicle to be parked within said no parking zone shall be
subject to the penalties as provided in section
11-2-8 of this chapter.
Main Street:
There is hereby established a "no parking zone" which shall consist of the now
existing two (2) parking spaces on the west side of Main Street, immediately
following said street's intersection with West Beardstown Street; said zone
shall be properly marked and identified by the elimination of the existing
parking space markings and replaced with such markings and signage customarily
used to establish "no parking zones" so as to properly apprise motor vehicle
traffic of said zone. In eliminating said spots, the southernmost remaining
spot shall be designated and properly marked as a loading zone for the purpose
of temporary parking not to exceed fifteen (15) minutes. Operators of motor
vehicles parked in the "no parking zone" or in violation of the time
restrictions for the loading zone shall be subject to a fine of one hundred
fifty dollars ($150.00), plus court costs.
There is hereby established a "no parking zone" which shall consist of all that
part along Main Street along the easterly side of traffic moving in a northerly
direction, between the intersections of Main Street and Jefferson Street and
Main Street and Beardstown Street; said zone shall be properly marked and
identified with such markings and/or signage customarily used to establish "no
parking zones" so as to properly apprise motor vehicle traffic of said zone.
Operators of motor vehicles parked in the "no parking zone" shall be subject to
a fine of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00), plus court costs.
Route 125:
All parking is hereafter prohibited at all locations on Route 125 over which
the city has jurisdiction. (Ord., 8-4-1969; amd. Ord., 7-1-1985; Ord., 1-5-
1987; 2009 Code; Ord. 11-13, 11-14-2011; Ord. 12-16, 8-13-2012)
11-2-5: LIMITED PARKING ON CERTAIN STREETS AND PLACES:
From and after the effective date of this chapter it shall be unlawful for any
vehicle, except fire, police, ambulance or other emergency vehicles, in times
of emergencies or drills therefore, to park along the north side of Springfield
Street, in the five parking spaces in front of the grocery store now known as
the Virginia Market, and lying between the intersection of Front and
Springfield Streets to the west and the curb cut on east side of the store for
more than thirty (30) minutes from Monday through Friday from eight o’clock (8:
00) a.m. through three o’clock (3:00) p.m. (Ord. 2020-07, 5-11-2020)
11-2-6: PARKING TRUCKS, TRACTORS AND COMMERCIAL VEHICLES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any bus, truck, tractor, tractor and trailer
or trailer and load, or any commercial vehicle to park on either side of the
following streets, except when loading or unloading: (Ord., 11-4-1946; amd.
2009 Code)
 
Street                 Location
East Beardstown Street Main Street east to Cass Street
South Front Street     Beardstown Street south to city parking lot
West Beardstown Street Front Street west to the alley
 
(Ord., 11-4-1946)
   B.   It shall be unlawful to park any semitruck, tractor or trailer upon any
street within the city. Violations of this subsection shall be punishable by
the imposition of a fine in an amount not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor
greater than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (Ord., 7-2-1990; amd. 2009
Code)
11-2-7: LOADING AND UNLOADING:
Special no parking spaces in front of shipping entrances and the entrances to
places of worship, hotels, theaters, office buildings or other buildings where
a large number of people are accustomed to gather may be provided and
established by compliance with the following conditions: (1925 Code § 35-14;
amd. 2009 Code)
   A.   Any owner or occupant of such building adjacent to a street or alley
desiring a certain no parking space immediately in front of the entrance to
such building shall make application to the City Council setting forth all
relevant information and stating the number of feet and the time desired for
such purpose.
   B.   The City Council shall have authority to grant or refuse such
application in their discretion, or to grant the same with such restrictions or
limitations as they may fix.
   C.   In case such application is granted, the City Council shall issue to
the applicant a permit setting forth the location of such no parking space, the
number of feet frontage and the time limits fixed and such other limitations as
may be pertinent. Such permit may at any time be withdrawn or further limited
by the Council.
   D.   To enforce the provisions of the permit, the holder of the same shall
have the right to place "no parking" signs on the sidewalk within the time
limit fixed in such permit, marking the limits of such no parking space. Such
signs shall be of the exact size, character and description required by the
City Council, but shall be provided at the expense of the holder of the permit,
and shall bear the number of the permit issued. (1925 Code § 35-14)
11-2-8: PARKING FOR PERSONS WITH DISABILITIES:
   A.   Designation Of Spots: The following parking spaces are designated as
parking spaces for persons with disabilities:
The four (4) parking spaces immediately west of the existing handicapped
parking space in front of the Presbyterian church.
The parking space immediately in front of the City Hall, 153 South Front
Street, Virginia, Illinois.
Two (2) additional parking spots on the north side of Beardstown Street,
between Front Street and Main Street, and as close as practical to an existing
wheelchair ramp located on the sidewalk running parallel to Beardstown Street.
One additional parking spot on the west side of Beardstown Street, between
Front Street and Main Street, and as close as practical to an existing
crosswalk running across Beardstown Street. (Ord. 03-05, 8-11-2003; amd. Ord.
05-01, 1-10-2005; Ord. 12-19, 10-9-2012; Ord. 2016-11, 10-10-2016)
   B.   Usage And Penalty: Parking in said spots is permitted only when the
disabled person is present, the vehicle is being used for his/her
transportation, and the persons with a disability parking permit issued by the
appropriate governmental body is displayed. The fine for unauthorized use of
said parking spots shall be two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00). (Ord. 12-19,
10-9-2012)
11-2-9: PAYMENT OF FINES; RESPONSIBILITY FOR ADDITIONAL COSTS:
The fines imposed for parking violations shall be paid within forty eight (48)
hours of the notice of the violation. In any action brought by the City which
results in the successful collection of unpaid parking fines, the City shall be
entitled to the payment of reasonable attorney fees. (Ord., 2-1-1988; amd. 2009
Code)
11-2-10: WINTER PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   The Virginia City Square, as referred in this section, shall be that
portion of Beardstown Street, Springfield Street, Main Street, and Front Street
as defined by the area within the intersections of said streets.
   B.   No vehicle shall park, stop or stand idle on the Virginia City Square
between the hours of six o'clock (6:00) P.M. and six o'clock (6:00) A.M., when
two inches (2") or more of snow has fallen until said square has been
completely plowed. The official depth for the purpose of this subsection shall
be determined by the City Public Works Director, whose determination shall be
final and not subject to appeal.
   C.   No vehicle shall park, stop or stand idle on the Virginia City Square
between the hours of six o'clock (6:00) P.M. and six o'clock (6:00) A.M., when
the National Weather Service forecast for the City predicts snowfall to meet or
exceed two inches (2") during any twenty four (24) hour period preceding,
including, or immediately following the commencement of said restricted time
period. For the purpose of this subsection only, the Public Works Director
shall post the start date and end date for parking restrictions called for by
this subsection, by placing notice of "winter parking restriction" at City Hall
or other conspicuous, public place located on said Virginia City Square.
   D.   Any vehicle parked in violation of this section shall be towed at the
vehicle owner's expense, which shall be, at a minimum, a one hundred dollar
($100.00) charge. Furthermore, any vehicle towed for violation of this section
shall not be released until all towing and storage charges are paid in full.
Storage charges shall accrue at the rate of twenty five dollars ($25.00) per
day, commencing the day following the day the vehicle was towed.
   E.   In addition to the penalties provided in this section, any violation of
this section is also punishable as provided under the City's General Penalty
Ordinance, section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 2015-15-02, 5-11-2015)
11-2-11: COMPACT VEHICLE PARKING:
   A.   A compact vehicle is any vehicle that has a combined passenger and
cargo volume of one hundred to one hundred nine (100-109) cubic feet.
   B.   The first three (3) parking spaces at the southeast corner of the
intersection of Front Street and Beardstown Street are hereby declared to be
Compact Vehicle Parking Spaces.
   C.   The City shall cause to be marked at the parking spaces and/or upon the
surface of the pavement, by signs, lines, markings, curbs, or other practical
manner, the size and limits of any parking spaces restricted for compact cars
or smaller vehicles.
   D.   It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle other than a compact vehicle
in or upon the parking spaces designated for compact vehicle parking.
   E.   It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle or trailer across any line or
marking or to park any vehicle or trailer in such a manner that part of the
vehicle extends over or across lines or markings designating the limit of the
compact vehicle parking space.
(Ord. 2024-5, 12-9-2024)
CHAPTER 3
VEHICLE EQUIPMENT AND CONDITION
SECTION:
11-3-1: Horn
11-3-2: Lights
11-3-3: Brakes
11-3-4: Noise Control
11-3-5: Weight Limit
11-3-1: HORN:
A person driving an automobile within the limits of the city must have same
properly equipped with a horn, bell or other device for signaling by sound, to
give warning of its approach. No horn, bell or other signaling device shall be
used except as necessary to give warning. Siren signaling devices shall not be
used on any vehicle except those operated by the police department, fire
department, the sheriff and authorized public utility vehicles when on
emergency calls. (1925 Code § 35-17)
11-3-2: LIGHTS:
The lights on all vehicles operated within the village shall be in compliance
with 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/12-201. (2009 Code)
11-3-3: BRAKES:
Every motor vehicle operated on the streets of the city shall be provided with
adequate brakes. (1925 Code § 35-17)
11-3-4: NOISE CONTROL:
   A.   Muffler Required; Noisy Vehicles Prohibited: Every motor vehicle,
except electric, operating on the streets of the city shall be equipped with an
adequate muffler which shall not be cut out when used on the streets. No person
operating a vehicle shall permit the pipes, muffler or other devices to emit
sounds of exhaust in a loud and annoying manner, and all such vehicles shall be
operated in as noiseless a manner as possible. (1925 Code § 35-18)
   B.   Jake Brakes Prohibited: It is in the best interests of the city to
control unwanted noise throughout the city. The noise created by the use of
compression braking, also known as "jake brakes", by semitractors and large
trucks is disturbing to the citizens of Virginia, particularly in the evening
and early morning hours. The use of compression braking, also known as "jake
brakes", upon the streets and highways within the city limits is hereby
prohibited. (Ord., 2-7-2000; amd. 2009 Code)
11-3-5: WEIGHT LIMIT:
   A.   Weight Limit Established: The gross weight limit of any truck or other
motor vehicle, including its load, shall be a total weight not in excess of
twenty eight thousand (28,000) pounds.
   B.   Truck Routes: No person shall drive, operate or park any truck or other
motor vehicle having a gross weight in pounds, including the vehicle and its
load, in excess of twenty eight thousand (28,000) pounds in the city, except
streets designated as through state highways. However, this subsection does not
prohibit the driving, operating or parking of a motor vehicle on a residential
street if the most direct route is used for the purpose of making a local
delivery or local pick up within the city.
   C.   Enforcement: The enforcement of this section may be by either a
complaint or on information filed in the circuit court of the county in the
Cass County courthouse, located in the city. (Ord., 1-8-1979; amd. 2009 Code)
CHAPTER 4
ABANDONED VEHICLES
SECTION:
11-4-1: Definitions
11-4-2: Abandonment Prohibited; Removal Authorized
11-4-3: Duty To Notify Police Of Abandoned, Unclaimed Vehicle
11-4-4: Abandoned, Wrecked Vehicle On Street
11-4-5: Records Of Towed Vehicles
11-4-6: Owner Unknown
11-4-7: Reclamation Of Vehicle
11-4-8: Sale And Disposal Of Vehicle
11-4-9: Disposition Of Revenue
11-4-10: Nonliability Of Police And Towing Service
11-4-11: Violation; Penalty
11-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: All motor vehicles or other vehicles in a state of disrepair
rendering the vehicle incapable of being driven in its condition; or any motor
vehicle or other vehicle that has not been moved or used for seven (7)
consecutive days or more and is apparently deserted.
ANTIQUE VEHICLE: A motor vehicle that is more than twenty five (25) years of
age, or a bona fide replica thereof, and which is driven on the highways only
going to and returning from an antique auto show or an exhibition, or for
servicing or demonstration, or a firefighting vehicle more than twenty (20)
years old which is not used as firefighting equipment but is used only for the
purpose of exhibition or demonstration.
HIGHWAY: Any street, alley or public way within the city. (Ord., 6-1-1970; amd.
2009 Code)
11-4-2: ABANDONMENT PROHIBITED; REMOVAL AUTHORIZED:
The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle, or any part thereof, on
any highway in the city is unlawful and subject to the penalties as set forth
herein. The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part thereof
on private or public property, other than a highway, in view of the general
public, anywhere in the city is unlawful except on property of the owner or
bailee of such abandoned vehicle. A motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part
thereof so abandoned on private property may be authorized for removal by or
upon the order of the chief of the police department after a waiting period of
seven (7) days or more has expired. (Ord., 6-1-1970)
11-4-3: DUTY TO NOTIFY POLICE OF ABANDONED, UNCLAIMED VEHICLE:
When an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor vehicle or other motor
vehicle comes into the temporary possession or custody of a person in this
state not the owner of the vehicle, such person shall immediately notify the
police department when the vehicle is within the corporate limits of the city.
Upon receipt of such notification, the chief of police shall authorize a towing
service to remove and take possession of the abandoned, lost, stolen or
unclaimed motor vehicle or other vehicle. The towing service will safely keep
the towed vehicle and its contents and maintain a record of the tow until the
vehicle is claimed by the owner or any other person legally entitled to
possession thereof or until it is disposed of as provided in this chapter.
(Ord., 6-1-1970)
11-4-4: ABANDONED, WRECKED VEHICLE ON STREET:
   A.   When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is abandoned on a highway in the
city ten (10) hours or more, its removal by a towing service may be authorized
by order of the chief of police.
   B.   When an abandoned, unattended, wrecked, burned or partially dismantled
motor vehicle or other vehicle is creating a traffic hazard because of its
position in relation to the highway or its physical appearance is causing the
impeding of traffic, its immediate removal from the highway by a towing service
may be authorized by order of the chief of police.
   C.   When a vehicle removed from either public or private property is
authorized by order of the chief of police, the owner of the vehicle will be
responsible for all towing costs. (Ord., 6-1-1970)
11-4-5: RECORDS OF TOWED VEHICLES:
When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is authorized to be towed away, the
police department shall keep and maintain a record of the vehicle towed,
listing the color, year of manufacture, manufacturer's trade name,
manufacturer's series name, body style, vehicle identification number and
license plate year and number and registration sticker year and number
displayed on the vehicle. The record shall also include the date and hour of
tow, location towed from, location towed to, reason for towing and the name of
the officer authorizing the tow. (Ord., 6-1-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
11-4-6: OWNER UNKNOWN:
   A.   When the police department does not know the identity of the registered
owner, lien holder or other legally entitled person, it will cause the motor
vehicle registration records of the state of Illinois to be searched by a
directed communication to the secretary of state for the purpose of obtaining
the required ownership information.
   B.   The police department will cause the stolen motor vehicle files of the
Illinois state police to be searched by a directed communication to the
Illinois state police for stolen or wanted information on the vehicle. When the
Illinois state police files are searched with negative results, the information
contained in the National Crime Information Center (NCIC) files will be
searched by the Illinois state police. The information determined from these
record searches will be used by the police department in sending a notification
by certified mail to the registered owner, lien holder or legally entitled
person advising where the vehicle is held, requesting a disposition be made and
setting forth public sale information.
   C.   When the registered owner, lien holder or other person legally entitled
to the possession of a motor vehicle or other vehicle cannot be identified from
the registration files of this state or from the registration files of a
foreign state, if applicable, the police department shall notify the Illinois
state police for the purpose of identifying the vehicle's owner, lien holder or
other person legally entitled to the possession of the vehicle. The information
obtained by the Illinois state police will be immediately forwarded to the
police department for notification of owner, lien holder or other person
legally entitled to the possession of the vehicle. (Ord., 6-1-1970; amd. 2009
Code)
11-4-7: RECLAMATION OF VEHICLE:
Any time before a motor vehicle or other vehicle is sold at public sale or
disposed of as provided herein, the owner, lien holder or other person legally
entitled to its possession may reclaim the vehicle by presenting to the police
department proof of ownership or proof of the right to possession of the
vehicle. No vehicle shall be released to the owner, lien holder or other person
under this section until all towing and storage charges have been paid. (Ord.,
6-1-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
11-4-8: SALE AND DISPOSAL OF VEHICLE:
   A.   Vehicles Seven Years Of Age Or Newer:
      1.   Known Owner: Whenever an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor
vehicle or other vehicle seven (7) years of age or newer remains unclaimed by
the registered owner, lien holder or other legally entitled person for a period
of thirty (30) days after notice has been given as provided herein, the police
department shall cause it to be sold at public sale to the highest bidder.
Notice of the time and place of the sale shall be posted in a conspicuous place
for at least ten (10) days prior to the sale on the premises where the vehicle
has been impounded. At least ten (10) days prior to the sale, the police
department shall cause a notice of the time and place of the sale to be sent by
certified mail to the registered owner, lien holder or other legally entitled
person. Such notice shall contain a complete description of the vehicle to be
sold and what steps must be taken by any legally entitled person to reclaim the
vehicle. In those instances where the certified notification specified herein
has been returned by the postal authorities to the police department, due to
the addressee having moved or being unknown at the address obtained from the
registration records of this state, the sending of a second certified notice
will not be required.
      2.   Unknown Owner: When the identity of the registered owner, lien
holder or other legally entitled persons of an abandoned, lost or unclaimed
vehicle of seven (7) years of age or newer cannot be determined by any means
provided for in this chapter, the vehicle may be sold as provided herein or
disposed of in the manner authorized by this chapter without notice to any
person whose identity cannot be determined.
   B.   Vehicles Older Than Seven Years: When an abandoned vehicle of more than
seven (7) years of age is impounded as specified by this chapter, or when any
such vehicle is towed at the request or with the consent of the owner or
operator and is subsequently abandoned, it will be kept in custody or storage
for a minimum of ten (10) days for the purpose of determining the identity of
the registered owner, lien holder, or other legally entitled persons and
contacting the registered owner, lien holder, or other legally entitled persons
by the U.S. mail, public service or in person for a determination of
disposition and an examination of the state police stolen vehicle files for
theft and wanted information. At the expiration of the ten (10) day period,
without the benefit of disposition information being received from the
registered owner, lien holder, or other legally entitled persons, the vehicle
shall be disposed of as junk or salvage.
   C.   Records Kept: When a motor vehicle or other vehicle in the custody of
the police department is reclaimed by the registered owner, lien holder or
other legally entitled person, or when the vehicle is sold at public sale or
otherwise disposed of, as provided in this chapter, a report of the transaction
will be maintained by the police department for a period of one year from the
date of the sale or disposal. (Ord., 6-1-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
   D.   Antique Vehicles Exempt: A motor vehicle or other vehicle classified as
an antique vehicle is excluded from the provisions of this section. (Ord., 6-1-
1970)
11-4-9: DISPOSITION OF REVENUE:
When a vehicle located within the corporate limits of the city is authorized to
be towed away by the chief of police and disposed of as set forth in this
chapter, the proceeds of the public sale or disposition, after the deduction of
towing, storage and processing charges, shall be deposited in the city
treasury. (Ord., 6-1-1970)
11-4-10: NONLIABILITY OF POLICE AND TOWING SERVICE:
Any police officer or towing service owner, operator or employee shall not be
held to answer or be liable for damages in any action brought by the registered
owner, former registered owner or his legal representative, lien holder, or any
other person legally entitled to the possession of a motor vehicle or other
vehicle when the vehicle was processed and sold or disposed of as provided by
this chapter. (Ord., 6-1-1970; amd. 2009 Code)
11-4-11: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. A separate offense shall be deemed committed for each day
such violation is committed or permitted to continue. (Ord., 6-1-1970; amd.
2009 Code)
CHAPTER 5
GOLF CARTS, ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLES (ATV) AND UTILITY-TERRAIN VEHICLES (UTV)
SECTION:
11-5-1: Definitions
11-5-2: Vehicle Requirements
11-5-3: Restrictions
11-5-4: Operation Of Golf Carts/ Recreational Off-Highway Vehicles/UTVs
11-5-5: Annual Registration Of Golf Carts And Recreational Off-Highway
Vehicles/UTVs
11-5-6: Inspection Of Vehicles
11-5-7: Mandatory Insurance
11-5-8: Operation Limited To Licensed Drivers
11-5-9: Other Laws, Regulations And Ordinances
11-5-10: Use Under The Influence
11-5-11: Convictions
11-5-12: Penalty
11-5-13: Waiver Of Fee
11-5-14: Prior Ordinances
11-5-15: Invalidity
11-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words, terms and titles shall have the
following meanings:
 
                                   Any motorized off-highway device,
                                   designed to travel primarily off-highway,
                                   fifty (50) inches or less in width,
                                   having a manufacturer's dry weight of one
                                   thousand five hundred (1,500) pounds or

                                   saddle for operator use, and handlebars
                                   or steering wheel, for steering control,

                                   Vehicle Code.
                                   Any motorized off highway device designed
                                   to travel primarily off-highway, sixty-
                                   four (64) inches or less in width, having
                                   a manufacturer's dry weight of two
                                   thousand (2,000) pounds or less,
RECREATIONAL OFF-HIGHWAY VEHICLES/ traveling on four (4) or more non-highway
UTILITY TERRAIN VEHICLES (UTV):    tires, designed with a non-straddle seat
                                   and a steering wheel for steering
                                   control, except equipment such as
                                   lawnmowers defined by 625 ILCS 5/1.168.8
                                   and5/11-1426.l(a)(4) of the Illinois
                                   Vehicle Code and go-carts. (Ord. 2022-01,
                                   1-10-2022)
 
11-5-2: VEHICLE REQUIREMENTS:
All vehicles allowed to operate on city streets pursuant to this chapter shall
be equipped with all of the safety systems and equipment as required by the
Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 ILCS 5/11-1426.1, including: brakes, a steering
apparatus, tires, a rearview mirror, red reflectorized warning devices in the
front and rear, a slow moving emblem on the rear of the vehicle as required in
Section 12-709 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 ILCS 5/12-709, a headlight
that emits a white light visible from a distance of five hundred (500) feet to
the front, a tail lamp that emits a red light visible from at least one hundred
(100) feet from the rear, brake lights, turn signals, a windshield, and any and
all other safety equipment required to be installed and operational on such
vehicles as set forth in the said statute. No vehicle can be operated with more
people on board than designed by the manufacturer. Each occupant must be on
their own seat. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-3: RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Golf Carts and UTV s and all other vehicles that do not meet the
requirements set forth in this chapter are not authorized on the roadways of
the City of Virginia.
   B.   ATVs are not authorized on the roadways or within the City limits of
the City of Virginia, even if the ATV would otherwise meet the requirements set
forth in this chapter. Notwithstanding the preceding restriction, ATVs may be
used for snow removal within the City limits, provided that such ATVs are
transported, and not driven, to the snow removal site. ATVs used for snow
removal need not be covered by mandatory vehicle insurance, but must be covered
under a farm, home, or non-highway vehicle insurance policy issued with
coverage amounts no less than the minimum amounts set for bodily injury or
death and for destruction of property under Section 7-203 of the Illinois
Vehicle Code. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-4: OPERATION OF GOLF CARTS/RECREATIONAL OFF-HIGHWAY VEHICLES/UTVS:
   A.   Subject to the requirements of Section 11-1426.1 of the Illinois
Vehicle Code, 625 ILCS 5/11-1426.1, which are hereby adopted and incorporated
by reference by the City Council of the City of Virginia and of the provisions
of this chapter, drivers properly licensed to operate motor vehicles on the
roadways of the City of Virginia AND who are sixteen (16) years of age are
allowed to operate golf carts and/or UTVs under this chapter on the roadways of
the City of Virginia having a posted speed limit of thirty-five (35) miles per
hour or less. Any such vehicle must, however, abide by all City speed limits,
as well as all other traffic laws and rules of the road in effect from time to
time.
   B.   Golfcarts and UTV s are not allowed on the City sidewalks, parks,
Illinois State Route 78, and Illinois State Route 125 in the City of Virginia.
      1.   However, golf carts and UTVs may cross Illinois State Route 78 at
any intersection with a stop sign or traffic light ( except for those streets
constituting part of the Town Square as set forth in Paragraph C below). Golf
carts and UTVs must come to a complete stop before crossing, and must cross
Route 78 at a ninety (90)-degree angle.
      2.   Golf carts and/or UTVs may cross Illinois Route 125 at the following
intersections:
         a.   Illinois Route 125 and Duncan Street; or
         b.   Illinois Route 125 and County Shed Road. Golf carts and UTVs must
come to a complete stop before crossing, and must cross Route 125 at a ninety
(90)-degree angle.
   C.   No golf cart or UTV shall operate on or around the Town Square. The
Town Square shall be defined as Front Street from the intersection of Front and
Beardstown Streets running northerly to Springfield Street at the intersection
of Springfield and Front Streets, thence easterly along Springfield Street to
the intersection of Main Street (Illinois Route 78), then southerly along Main
Street to the intersection of Main and Beardstown Streets, thence westerly on
Beardstown Street to the intersection of Beardstown and Front Streets.
   D.   Golf carts and UTVs are allowed on the designated areas between the
hours of six o’clock (6:00) a.m. through ten o’clock (10:00) p.m. (Ord. 2022-
01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-5: ANNUAL REGISTRATION OF GOLF CARTS AND RECREATIONAL OFF-HIGHWAY
VEHICLES/UTVS:
No vehicle authorized under this title and chapter shall be operated on any
street or alley in the City of Virginia unless the owner(s) thereof shall have
first registered such vehicle with the City of Virginia in accordance with the
following requirements:
   A.   Registration of such vehicles shall be administered by the Chief of
Police of the City of Virginia, or his designee. An application for
registration may be made on a form prescribed by the City of Virginia. Said
form shall include a statement under oath or penalties of perjury that the
vehicle proposed to be registered meets the definition of the vehicles defined
by the state statute or in Section
11-5-1 of this chapter and shall be accompanied by an annual registration fee
of one hundred dollars ($100.00) and proof of liability insurance for said
vehicle having at least the same limits of coverage as required from time to
time for motor vehicles under the mandatory insurance law of the State of
Illinois.
   B.   Vehicles registered under this chapter and section of the City of
Virginia Municipal Code shall be issued a sticker from the City of Virginia
which shall be affixed to the rear of the vehicle and shall be viewable to a
police officer from outside of said vehicle.
   C.   The registration of said vehicle shall be effective for a period of one
calendar year and shall be renewed annually on January 2nd of each year in the
same manner as the original registration.
   D.   The registration of said vehicles shall not be transferrable in the
event of a change of ownership. A new registration fee will be required of the
new owner(s). No refund of the original registration fee is allowed in the
event of the change of ownership.
   E.   The registration of said vehicles shall be subject to revocation by the
Chief of Police of the City of Virginia in the event of a violation of the
requirements of Section 11-1426. l of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 ILCS 5/11-
1426.1, or any of the provisions of this chapter. A revocation of such
registration shall be made in writing and shall set forth the provision(s) of
the state statute or this chapter that has been violated. No refund of the
registration fee is allowed in the event of the revocation of said permit.
   F.   In the event that the registration of a vehicle is revoked due to a
failure to maintain the required liability insurance or the failure of the
condition of the vehicle to be in compliance with the state statute or this
chapter, including, but not limited to, maintaining the required safety
systems, the Chief of Police of the City, or his/her designee, in his/her
discretion, may reinstate the registration upon documentation or reinstatement
of the required insurance coverage or of the repair of modification of the
vehicle to cure any deficiencies, as applicable, if the Chief of Police of the
City of Virginia determines that the violation was not intentional and is not
likely to recur. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-6: INSPECTION OF VEHICLES:
Vehicles registered or proposed to be registered, pursuant to the provisions of
this chapter, shall be subject to inspection before being issued said
registration sticker. The inspection is only required for the first year of
registration or if a sticker lapses. Vehicle owners may obtain an inspection
form from the City of Virginia Police Department and provide that form to the
business conducting the inspection. Businesses must inspect and certify on the
City of Virginia Police Department form that the vehicle meets the required
inspection. The inspector must certify that the vehicle meets the definition as
set forth in the state statute or this chapter, particularly in connection with
the provisions for maintenance in operating condition of required safety
systems and equipment. The certifying business must be a business whose primary
function is the selling of golf carts and/or UTVs, or whose primary function is
the repair of mechanical vehicles. Alternately, and only if no such certifying
business exists within thirty-five (35) miles of the Virginia city limits, then
the owner of the golf cart or UTV may undertake a self inspection and self-
certify using the form provided by the City. Where such self certification
occurs, the owner self certifying is responsible for the truth and accuracy of
the certification and statements on the form, and any violation for improper
certification may result in the assessment of an increased fine and attorneys'
fees as well as permanent revocation of the permit. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-7: MANDATORY INSURANCE:
The owner of any vehicle registered under this chapter shall continuously
maintain liability insurance for said vehicle having at least the same limits
of coverage as required from time to time for motor vehicles under the
mandatory insurance law of the State of Illinois. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-8: OPERATION LIMITED TO LICENSED DRIVERS:
All persons who operate a vehicle under this chapter within the City of
Virginia must have a valid Illinois driver's license. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-9: OTHER LAWS, REGULATIONS AND ORDINANCES:
Vehicles registered under this chapter shall be operated at all times in
accordance with the provisions of the Illinois Vehicle Code, the rules of the
road contained therein, and any other laws, regulations or ordinances governing
the operation of motor vehicles in the City of Virginia as well as the laws,
regulations or ordinances specifically pertaining to vehicles operated under
this chapter and the operation thereof. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-10: USE UNDER THE INFLUENCE:
A person who drives, or is in actual physical control of, a vehicle authorized
under this chapter, on a roadway in the City of Virginia, while under the
influence of alcohol or drugs, is subject to the provision of Sections 11-500
through 11-502 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 ILCS 5/11-500 through 11-502.
Further, a violation of the provisions of this Section shall be cause for the
City of Virginia to revoke the permit of the authorized vehicle. Revocation may
occur even if a conviction for a statutory offense has not occurred. (Ord.
2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-11: CONVICTIONS:
Two (2) convictions of any authorized user herein of a vehicle authorized under
the provisions of this chapter for moving violations concerning such vehicle
shall cause the registration provided for herein to be revoked for at least one
(1) year. It shall be the City of Virginia's Chief of Police to determine if
the registration will be reinstated after the one (1) year revocation. If the
Chief of Police denies reinstatement, the applicant may appeal the decision to
the City Council. The City Council's decision on reinstatement shall be a final
administrative determination. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-12: PENALTY:
In addition to the revocation of the registration of a vehicle as provided in
this chapter, any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall
be subject to fines for each offense, as well as court costs and the City of
Virginia's attorney's fees. The amount of fines may be between one hundred
dollars ($100.00) through seven hundred and fifty dollars ($750.00) for each
offense. The provisions hereof for prosecuting violations of this chapter are
not intended in any way to supersede the provision of the Illinois Vehicle Code
involving the operation of said vehicles within the City of Virginia. (Ord.
2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-13: WAIVER OF FEE:
The provisions of this chapter shall apply to the use and operation of a
vehicle solely owned by a unit of local govermnent (i.e. City of Virginia,
Virginia Parks, etc.); however, the registration fee for such vehicles are
waived. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-14: PRIOR ORDINANCES:
All prior ordinances and amendments to ordinances which are inconsistent with
this chapter are hereby repealed. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
11-5-15: INVALIDITY:
If any section, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase of this chapter is
declared or held to be unconstitutional or invalid for any reason, the
remainder of this chapter shall not be affected thereby and shall rem. ain in
full force and effect. (Ord. 2022-01, 1-10-2022)
